Conversion of Wala al-Muwalat: Conditions and Legal Reasoning
Explains conversion conditions with analogical reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for legally converting wala al-muwalat and explain why the contract is non-binding using Hanafi qiyas.

Core Idea
Conversion of wala al-muwalat is permissible only before aql is paid and in the presence of the other patron.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on transferring wala al-muwalat from one patron to another. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, as explained by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, establishes that such conversion is allowed, but with specific conditions. The commentary reveals the underlying legal reasoning, comparing the contract to agency and partnership, and highlights the importance of the absence of blood-wit payment. Understanding this ruling deepens your grasp of how non-binding contracts operate in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is converting (tahawwul) wala al-muwalat from one patron to another. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) subject to conditions.
2
Extract the conditions from the text
Two conditions are explicitly stated: (1) the conversion must take place in the presence (bi mahdari) of the other patron, and (2) the original patron must not have paid blood-wit (aql) on behalf of the client.
The presence condition ensures mutual knowledge and consent; the aql condition prevents harm once the patron has incurred liability.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (talil)
The contract of wala al-muwalat is non-binding (ghayr lazim), like a bequest or agency. Since it is not binding, each party has the right to rescind, but rescission requires the other's knowledge to avoid potential harm (e.g., inheritance liability or mistaken blood-wit obligations).
The analogy to agency and partnership is used: those contracts are also non-binding and allow rescission with consent.
4
Analyze the exception: effect of aql
Once blood-wit is paid, the wala becomes confirmed (mu'akkad) because a third party's right attaches. At this point, conversion is no longer allowed.
This is analogous to a gift (hiba) that becomes binding after delivery; aql turns the gratuitous contract into a compensatory one.
5
Note the constructive rescission (faskh hukmi)
If the client contracts wala with a third party without the knowledge of the first patron, the first contract is automatically rescinded. This is a constructive rescission that does not require explicit knowledge.
This is similar to agency and partnership: if one partner enters a new partnership without the other's knowledge, the first partnership is dissolved by operation of law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وله أن يتحول منه إلى غيره بمحضر من الآخر ما لم يعقل عنه لأن العقد غير لازم كالوصية والوكالة ولكل واحد منهما أن يفسخه بعلم الآخر، فإن كان الآخر غائباً لا يملك فسخه وإن كان غير لازم لأن العقد تم لهما كما في الشركة والمضاربة والوكالة ولا يعرى عن ضرر لأنه ربما يموت الأسفل فيأخذ الأعلى ميراثه فيكون مضموناً عليه، أو يعقل الأسفل عبيداً على حسبان أن عقل عبيده على المولى الأعلى فيجب عليه وحده فيتضرر بذلك فلا يصح الفسخ إلا بمحضر من الآخر بخلاف ما إذا عقد الأسفل الموالاة مع غيره بغير محضر من حتى يصح وينفسخ العقد الأول لأنه فسخ حكمي فلا يشترط فيه العلم كما في الوكالة والمضاربة والشركة لأن الموالاة كالنسب إذا ثبت من شخص كونه مع غيره فينفسخ ضرورة، والمرأة في هذا كالرجل. وقوله ما لم يعقل عنه لأنه إذا عقل عنه ليس له أن يتحول إلى غيره لتأكده بتعلق حق الغير به لحصول المعقود به ولاتصال العصوبة ولأن ولاية التحول قبل أن يعقل عنه باعتبار أنه عقد تبرع، فإذا عقل عنه صار كالعوض في الهبة، وكذا لا يتحول ولده بعد ما تحمل الجناية عن أبيه، وكذا إن عقل عن ولده لم يكن لكل واحد منهما أن يتحول إلى غيره لأنهما كشخص واحد في حكم الولاء.
He, may God have mercy on him, said: (And he may transfer from it to another in the presence of the other, as long as he has not paid blood-wit for him) because the contract is not binding like a bequest and agency. Each of them may rescind it with the knowledge of the other. If the other is absent, he cannot rescind it even though it is not binding, because the contract was concluded for both of them as in partnership, mudaraba, and agency, and it is not free from harm because perhaps the lower one dies and the higher one takes his inheritance, thus becoming liable; or the lower one pays blood-wit for slaves thinking that their blood-wit is upon the higher master, and then it becomes obligatory upon him alone, and he is harmed by that. Hence rescission is only valid in the presence of the other. Unlike when the lower one contracts wala with another without the presence of [the first?], so that it becomes valid and the first contract is rescinded because it is a constructive rescission for which knowledge is not required, as in agency, mudaraba, and partnership, because wala is like lineage: if it is established from a person that he is with another, it is necessarily rescinded. And a woman is like a man in this. His saying 'as long as he has not paid blood-wit for him' means that if he has paid blood-wit for him, he cannot transfer to another because it becomes confirmed by the right of the third party attached to it due to the occurrence of the atoned act and the connection of patronage; and because the right to transfer before paying blood-wit is considered as a gratuitous contract, but once he pays blood-wit it becomes like a compensation in gift. Similarly, his child cannot transfer after the liability for injury has been borne by the father. And likewise, if he paid blood-wit for his child, neither of them can transfer to another because they are like one person in the ruling of wala.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the conversion (tahawwul) of wala al-muwalat. The matn states that a person can transfer his wala from one patron to another, provided the other patron is present and he has not yet paid blood-wit (aql) on behalf of the client. The commentary explains the reasoning: the contract of wala al-muwalat is not binding (ghayr lazim), similar to a bequest or agency. Each party can rescind it, but rescission requires the knowledge of the other party; if the other is absent, he cannot rescind alone due to potential harm (e.g., inheritance liability or blood-wit obligations). However, if the client (asfal) contracts wala with a third party without the knowledge of the first, the first contract is automatically rescinded by constructive rescission (faskh hukmi). The condition 'as long as he has not paid blood-wit' is explained: once blood-wit is paid, the wala becomes confirmed (mu'akkad) because a third party's right attaches, and the conversion right is lost. This also applies to the child of the client; if the father bore liability for the child, the child cannot transfer.

Key Terms
عقل (aql): Payment of blood-wit (diya) by the patron on behalf of the client.
فسخ حكمي (faskh hukmi): Constructive rescission occurring automatically without explicit knowledge or statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a person allowed to transfer his wala al-muwalat to another patron?
A) Anytime without conditions
B) Only after paying blood-wit
C) Before paying blood-wit and in the presence of the other patron
D) Only if the other patron is absent

Key Takeaway
Conversion of wala al-muwalat is allowed only before aql is paid and in the presence of the other patron, due to the non-binding nature of the contract.

Division with Shared Paths and Rights of Way
Hanafi rulings on dividing properties with path rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on dividing property when co-owners have unequal rights of way, and apply the conditions for valid division when a path is missing or shared.

Core Idea
A shared path can be divided unequally by consent; a missing path may be excused if the owner can create access or agrees.

When co-owners divide a house or land, the right of way is a critical factor. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules for dividing paths, including when one owner lacks access. This lesson explores the rules for division with shared paths, cases where no path exists, and the treatment of chambers and shared alleys.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property and right-of-way scenario
Determine whether the property has a path, who owns it, and whether the division includes unequal shares of the path.
Focus on whether the path is common or belongs to one party.
2
Check mutual consent
Division of non-ribawi property by mutual consent is valid even if shares are unequal. Confirm if all partners agreed.
Ribawi property cannot be divided unequally.
3
Evaluate cases of missing path
If a co-owner has no path, see if they can create access for a person without load. If not, check whether they knew about the lack of path; if known and consented, division is valid; otherwise void.
The text distinguishes ability to create access and knowledge.
4
Apply rules for opening doors in shared walls
In a closed alley or chamber, each owner may only open a door to the extent of their right of passage, not beyond. Shared paths cannot be used for new doors without right.
No harm to others is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سفل له علو وسفل مجرد وعلو مجرد قوم كل على حدة وقسم بالقيمة ويقبل شهادة . الطريق في الدار على التفاوت جاز وإن سهامهم في الدار متساوية لأن القسمة على التفاوت بالتراضي في غير الأموال الربوية جائزة، وإن كان ذلك أرضاً يرفع قدر ما يمر به نور لوقوع الكفاية به في المرور. ولم يذكر حكمه فيما إذا لم يكن له طريق وفي المحيط : ولو اقتسموا داراً فإذا لا طريق لأحدهم وقدر على أن يفتح في نصيبه طريقاً يمر فيه الرجل دون الحمولة جازت القسمة لأنها لم تتضمن تفويت منفعة، وإن لم يقدر ؛ ينظر إن لم يعلم أنه لا طريق له فالقسمة فاسدة، وإن علم أنه لا طريق له جازت القسمة لأنه رضي بهذه القسمة. دار في سكة غير نافذة اقتسموها على أن يفتح كل واحد باباً إلى السكة جاز ولا يمنعون منه لأنهم تصرفوا في خالص حقهم وهو الجدار ولا ضرر على غيرهم في ذلك مقصورة بين قوم طريقها في دار الآخر فاقتسموها فليس لكل واحد أن يفتح باباً المقصورة إلى الدار، وإنما من لهم طريق على مقدار الباب ولا يكون لهم حق المرور فيما سوى الطريق، وإن كان بجنب المقصورة دار لهم وقعت في قسمة رجل فأراد أحدهم أن يجعل الطريق إلى داره في هذه المقصورة لم يكن له ذلك طريق مشترك بين جماعة ليس لواحد منهم أن يفتح باباً لدار أخرى لا حق لها في هذه الطريق. ولو اقتسموا قرية فأصاب أحدهم قراح والآخر كرم والآخر بيوت جاز بتراضيهم، وإذا اقتسما كرم وفيه عنب وثمر ينظر ؛ إن قالا على أن النصف لفلان بكل قليل وكثير وما فيه من الأعشاب والثمار فهي مقسومة وإلا فهي على الشركة بينهما. دار وفيها طريق لآخر لا يمنعها عن قسمتها ويترك طريقه على عرض الباب العظمى، فإن باعوا الدار والطريق برضاهم ضرب صاحب الدار على مثلي ثمن الطريق وصاحب الممر بثلث الثمن لأن الطريق بينهم أثلاثاً إذا لم يعلم قدر الأنصباء فيكون الثمن بينهم أثلاثاً، وكذا إذا كان رقبة الطريق لاثنين وللآخر حق المرور. ومن مات منهم وتعددت ورثته اعتبر حقه كحق واحد، وإن لم يعرف أن الدار ميراث بينهم فالطريق على عدد الرؤوس وقسمة الطريق على عدد الرؤوس . ولو كان فيها طريق من ناحية وطريق لآخر من ناحية أخرى يعزل لهما طريق واحدة والطريق الواحد يكفي للمرور ولو اقتسموا داراً وفيها كنيف شارع إلى الطريق أو لم يحسب في ذرع الدار لأن الظلة والكنيف ليس لهما حق القرار على طريق العامة بل مستحق النقض، ومستحق النقض كالمنقوض ولكنهما يقومان على من وقعا في حيزه، ولا يحسبان في ذرعان الدار بعد قسمه الوالي وترك طريقاً للعامة فرأى الوالي بعد ذلك أن يعطي الطريق لواحد فينتفع بها ولا يضر بأهل الطريق جاز إن كانت المدينة له، وإن كانت للمسلمين ظلة لم يجز اهـ
A lower part that has an upper part, and a lower part alone, and an upper part alone: each is valued separately and divided by value. Testimony is accepted. The path in the house on a differential basis is permissible even if their shares in the house are equal, because division on a differential basis by mutual consent in non-ribawi property is permissible. If it is land that lifts the amount sufficient for light to pass through because sufficiency for passage is achieved. He did not mention its ruling when one has no path. In Al-Muhit: If they divide a house and one of them has no path and is able to open in his share a path through which a man can pass without a load, the division is permissible because it does not entail loss of benefit. If unable, consider: if it was not known that he had no path, the division is void; if it was known he had no path, the division is permissible because he consented to this division. A house in a closed alley: they divide it on the condition that each opens a door to the alley; it is permissible and they are not prevented, because they dispose of their pure right which is the wall, and there is no harm to others in that. A chamber among people whose path is in another's house; they divide it: it is not for each to open a door from the chamber to the house; only those who have a path have a right to the amount of the door, and they do not have a right of passage beyond the path. If adjacent to the chamber they have a house that fell into the share of a man, and one of them wants to make the path to his house in this chamber, he does not have that. A shared path among a group: none of them may open a door to another house that has no right to this path. If they divide a village and one gets a field, another a vineyard, another houses, it is permissible by their mutual consent. If they divide a vineyard with grapes and fruit, consider: if they said that half is for so-and-so with every little and much, and whatever is in it of plants and fruits, it is divided; otherwise it remains in partnership between them. A house with a path for another: it does not prevent its division, and its path is left on the width of the largest door. If they sell the house and the path by their consent, the owner of the house takes two-thirds of the price of the path, and the owner of the passage takes one-third because the path is between them in thirds if the amounts of shares are unknown; thus the price is between them in thirds. Likewise if the land of the path is owned by two and the other has a right of passage. If one of them dies and his heirs are multiple, his right is considered as one right. If it is not known that the house is inheritance between them, then the path is by the number of persons, and the division of the path is by the number of persons. If there is a path from one side and another path from another side, he sets aside for them one path, and a single path suffices for passage. If they divide a house and there is a toilet opening to the path, it is not counted in the measurement of the house because the canopy and toilet have no right of settlement on the public path; they are subject to demolition, and what is subject to demolition is like the demolished. But they are valued for the one in whose space they fall, and they are not counted in the measurements of the house. After the governor divides and leaves a path for the public, then the governor sees after that to give the path to one so that he benefits from it and does not harm the path people, it is permissible if the city belongs to him; if it belongs to the Muslims, a canopy is not permissible. End.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings from the chapter of division (qisma). The text discusses various scenarios: division of property with upper and lower parts is done by value, not by measure. A path in a house can be divided unequally by mutual consent even if the shares are equal, because non-ribawi property can be divided unequally with agreement. When there is no path, the division is valid if the one without a path can create a passage for a person (without load) or if he knowingly consents. Houses in a dead-end alley: each can open a door to the alley; they have a right to the wall. For a chamber with a path through another's house, each partner may only open a door to the extent of their right of passage. A shared path cannot be used to open a door for another property without right. Division of a village with different types of land (field, vineyard, houses) is valid by mutual consent. In dividing a vineyard, if the partners include fruits and plants in the division explicitly, it is divided; otherwise it remains common. If a house has a path for another, the division proceeds and the path is left at the width of the largest door. The price of the path is divided according to shares when unknown. If a house has a toilet or canopy on the public path, it is not counted in the area because it is temporary; but it is valued for the owner. The governor may grant use of part of a public path to an individual if it does not harm the public and the land belongs to him; if the land belongs to the Muslims, it is not permissible.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Division of jointly owned property into separate shares among co-owners.
طريق (tariq): A path or right of way that allows access to a property.
ظلة (zullah): A canopy or covering that projects over a public path; it is subject to demolition if it obstructs.
كنيف (kanif): A toilet or latrine that opens onto a public path; it is not counted in the area of the house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a co-owner in a house division has no path and cannot open any passage, what makes the division valid?
A) If the other co-owners agree to give him a path after division.
B) If he gives up his share of the house.
C) If he knew about the lack of path and still consented to the division.
D) If the division is done by a judge.

Key Takeaway
Division of a shared path can be unequal by mutual consent; a missing path can be compensated by ability to create minimal access or knowing consent.

Division of Mixed Property and Price Calculations
Hanafi rulings on dividing villages, vineyards with fruit, and path price calculations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi rules for dividing villages with different land types, vineyards with fruit, and calculating the price of a path when part of it is sold.

Core Idea
Dividing mixed property types is valid by consent; fruit may be included in division by explicit agreement; path prices split by shares when unknown.

When co-owners divide a village or vineyard, the types of property may differ, and the inclusion of crops must be explicit. Additionally, if a house with a path is sold, the price distribution follows the shares of the path. This lesson covers these scenarios and the calculation rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property mix
Determine if the division involves different categories like field, vineyard, houses. Such division is permissible by mutual consent.
Consent is key; no requirement of equal value unless ribawi.
2
Check inclusion of fruits and plants
If dividing a vineyard with grapes and fruit, the fruits are divided only if explicitly stated; otherwise they remain common.
The text: 'if they said that half is for so-and-so with every little and much, and whatever is in it of plants and fruits, it is divided; otherwise it remains in partnership.'
3
Handle a house with a path another
Division of a house that has a path for another is not prevented; the path is left at the width of the largest door. If sold, the price is split according to shares.
The path width is determined by the largest existing door.
4
Calculate path price when shares unknown
If the path is sold with the house, the owner of the house takes two-thirds and the owner of the passage one-third because the path is between them in thirds when shares are unknown. This applies also when the path land is owned by two and a third has passage right.
The ratio is based on three shares: two for the house owner (who owns the path land?) Actually text: 'صاحب الدار على مثلي ثمن الطريق وصاحب الممر بثلث الثمن'.
5
Treat deceased co-owners and unknown inheritance
If one co-owner dies, his right is considered one right even with multiple heirs. If it's unknown whether the house is inheritance or not, the path is divided per head (number of persons).
The path is divided by heads, not by shares of the house.

Source Text

كان ذلك أرضاً يرفع قدر ما يمر به نور لوقوع الكفاية به في المرور. ولم يذكر حكمه فيما إذا لم يكن له طريق وفي المحيط : ولو اقتسموا داراً فإذا لا طريق لأحدهم وقدر على أن يفتح في نصيبه طريقاً يمر فيه الرجل دون الحمولة جازت القسمة لأنها لم تتضمن تفويت منفعة، وإن لم يقدر ؛ ينظر إن لم يعلم أنه لا طريق له فالقسمة فاسدة، وإن علم أنه لا طريق له جازت القسمة لأنه رضي بهذه القسمة. دار في سكة غير نافذة اقتسموها على أن يفتح كل واحد باباً إلى السكة جاز ولا يمنعون منه لأنهم تصرفوا في خالص حقهم وهو الجدار ولا ضرر على غيرهم في ذلك مقصورة بين قوم طريقها في دار الآخر فاقتسموها فليس لكل واحد أن يفتح باباً المقصورة إلى الدار، وإنما من لهم طريق على مقدار الباب ولا يكون لهم حق المرور فيما سوى الطريق، وإن كان بجنب المقصورة دار لهم وقعت في قسمة رجل فأراد أحدهم أن يجعل الطريق إلى داره في هذه المقصورة لم يكن له ذلك طريق مشترك بين جماعة ليس لواحد منهم أن يفتح باباً لدار أخرى لا حق لها في هذه الطريق. ولو اقتسموا قرية فأصاب أحدهم قراح والآخر كرم والآخر بيوت جاز بتراضيهم، وإذا اقتسما كرم وفيه عنب وثمر ينظر ؛ إن قالا على أن النصف لفلان بكل قليل وكثير وما فيه من الأعشاب والثمار فهي مقسومة وإلا فهي على الشركة بينهما. دار وفيها طريق لآخر لا يمنعها عن قسمتها ويترك طريقه على عرض الباب العظمى، فإن باعوا الدار والطريق برضاهم ضرب صاحب الدار على مثلي ثمن الطريق وصاحب الممر بثلث الثمن لأن الطريق بينهم أثلاثاً إذا لم يعلم قدر الأنصباء فيكون الثمن بينهم أثلاثاً، وكذا إذا كان رقبة الطريق لاثنين وللآخر حق المرور. ومن مات منهم وتعددت ورثته اعتبر حقه كحق واحد، وإن لم يعرف أن الدار ميراث بينهم فالطريق على عدد الرؤوس وقسمة الطريق على عدد الرؤوس . ولو كان فيها طريق من ناحية وطريق لآخر من ناحية أخرى يعزل لهما طريق واحدة والطريق الواحد يكفي للمرور ولو اقتسموا داراً وفيها كنيف شارع إلى الطريق أو لم يحسب في ذرع الدار لأن الظلة والكنيف ليس لهما حق القرار على طريق العامة بل مستحق النقض، ومستحق النقض كالمنقوض ولكنهما يقومان على من وقعا في حيزه، ولا يحسبان في ذرعان الدار بعد قسمه الوالي وترك طريقاً للعامة فرأى الوالي بعد ذلك أن يعطي الطريق لواحد فينتفع بها ولا يضر بأهل الطريق جاز إن كانت المدينة له، وإن كانت للمسلمين ظلة لم يجز اهـ
A lower part that has an upper part, and a lower part alone, and an upper part alone: each is valued separately and divided by value. Testimony is accepted. The path in the house on a differential basis is permissible even if their shares in the house are equal, because division on a differential basis by mutual consent in non-ribawi property is permissible. If it is land that lifts the amount sufficient for light to pass through because sufficiency for passage is achieved. He did not mention its ruling when one has no path. In Al-Muhit: If they divide a house and one of them has no path and is able to open in his share a path through which a man can pass without a load, the division is permissible because it does not entail loss of benefit. If unable, consider: if it was not known that he had no path, the division is void; if it was known he had no path, the division is permissible because he consented to this division. A house in a closed alley: they divide it on the condition that each opens a door to the alley; it is permissible and they are not prevented, because they dispose of their pure right which is the wall, and there is no harm to others in that. A chamber among people whose path is in another's house; they divide it: it is not for each to open a door from the chamber to the house; only those who have a path have a right to the amount of the door, and they do not have a right of passage beyond the path. If adjacent to the chamber they have a house that fell into the share of a man, and one of them wants to make the path to his house in this chamber, he does not have that. A shared path among a group: none of them may open a door to another house that has no right to this path. If they divide a village and one gets a field, another a vineyard, another houses, it is permissible by their mutual consent. If they divide a vineyard with grapes and fruit, consider: if they said that half is for so-and-so with every little and much, and whatever is in it of plants and fruits, it is divided; otherwise it remains in partnership between them. A house with a path for another: it does not prevent its division, and its path is left on the width of the largest door. If they sell the house and the path by their consent, the owner of the house takes two-thirds of the price of the path, and the owner of the passage takes one-third because the path is between them in thirds if the amounts of shares are unknown; thus the price is between them in thirds. Likewise if the land of the path is owned by two and the other has a right of passage. If one of them dies and his heirs are multiple, his right is considered as one right. If it is not known that the house is inheritance between them, then the path is by the number of persons, and the division of the path is by the number of persons. If there is a path from one side and another path from another side, he sets aside for them one path, and a single path suffices for passage. If they divide a house and there is a toilet opening to the path, it is not counted in the measurement of the house because the canopy and toilet have no right of settlement on the public path; they are subject to demolition, and what is subject to demolition is like the demolished. But they are valued for the one in whose space they fall, and they are not counted in the measurements of the house. After the governor divides and leaves a path for the public, then the governor sees after that to give the path to one so that he benefits from it and does not harm the path people, it is permissible if the city belongs to him; if it belongs to the Muslims, a canopy is not permissible. End.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings from the chapter of division (qisma). The text discusses various scenarios: division of property with upper and lower parts is done by value, not by measure. A path in a house can be divided unequally by mutual consent even if the shares are equal, because non-ribawi property can be divided unequally with agreement. When there is no path, the division is valid if the one without a path can create a passage for a person (without load) or if he knowingly consents. Houses in a dead-end alley: each can open a door to the alley; they have a right to the wall. For a chamber with a path through another's house, each partner may only open a door to the extent of their right of passage. A shared path cannot be used to open a door for another property without right. Division of a village with different types of land (field, vineyard, houses) is valid by mutual consent. In dividing a vineyard, if the partners include fruits and plants in the division explicitly, it is divided; otherwise it remains common. If a house has a path for another, the division proceeds and the path is left at the width of the largest door. The price of the path is divided according to shares when unknown. If a house has a toilet or canopy on the public path, it is not counted in the area because it is temporary; but it is valued for the owner. The governor may grant use of part of a public path to an individual if it does not harm the public and the land belongs to him; if the land belongs to the Muslims, it is not permissible.

Key Terms
قراح (qirah): A field or agricultural land.
كرم (karm): Vineyard.
مثلي (mithli): Two times; in context, two-thirds (since two-thirds is mathalay al-thulth?). Actually the text says 'ضرب صاحب الدار على مثلي ثمن الطريق' meaning two parts? In translation, two-thirds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a house with a path is sold by consent and the path shares are unknown, how is the price split?
A) Equally between all owners.
B) Owner of the house gets two-thirds, owner of passage gets one-third.
C) Based on the number of doors.
D) Only the path owner takes the price.

Key Takeaway
Mixed property division is valid by consent; fruits require explicit inclusion; path price defaults to thirds when shares unknown.

Rulings on Toilets, Canopies, and Public Paths
Hanafi ruling on counting toilets/canopies in house area and governor's powers over public paths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why toilets and canopies on public paths are not counted in the area measurement of a house, and apply the rule for a governor granting use of public path land.

Core Idea
Toilets and canopies on public paths are temporary structures not counted in area; the governor may grant use of public land only if he owns the city.

When dividing a house that has a toilet or canopy opening onto a public path, these structures are not considered part of the built area because they are subject to demolition. Additionally, the governor's authority over public paths is limited: he may give a portion for private benefit only if he owns the city; otherwise it is not permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure on the public path
Toilets (kanif) and canopies (zullah) that project onto the public path are considered temporary because they have no permanent right over public land.
They are subject to demolition at any time by the authorities.
2
Apply the ruling for measurement
When measuring the house for division, these structures are not counted in the area (dhira'). They are valued separately for the person in whose portion they fall.
The text: 'ولا يحسبان في ذرعان الدار'.
3
Determine the governor's authority over public paths
If the governor divided the property and left a public path, he cannot later give that path to an individual unless the city belongs to him (the governor). If the city belongs to the Muslims (general public), he cannot grant a canopy or similar benefit.
This prevents encroachment on public property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سفل له علو وسفل مجرد وعلو مجرد قوم كل على حدة وقسم بالقيمة ويقبل شهادة . الطريق في الدار على التفاوت جاز وإن سهامهم في الدار متساوية لأن القسمة على التفاوت بالتراضي في غير الأموال الربوية جائزة، وإن كان ذلك أرضاً يرفع قدر ما يمر به نور لوقوع الكفاية به في المرور. ولم يذكر حكمه فيما إذا لم يكن له طريق وفي المحيط : ولو اقتسموا داراً فإذا لا طريق لأحدهم وقدر على أن يفتح في نصيبه طريقاً يمر فيه الرجل دون الحمولة جازت القسمة لأنها لم تتضمن تفويت منفعة، وإن لم يقدر ؛ ينظر إن لم يعلم أنه لا طريق له فالقسمة فاسدة، وإن علم أنه لا طريق له جازت القسمة لأنه رضي بهذه القسمة. دار في سكة غير نافذة اقتسموها على أن يفتح كل واحد باباً إلى السكة جاز ولا يمنعون منه لأنهم تصرفوا في خالص حقهم وهو الجدار ولا ضرر على غيرهم في ذلك مقصورة بين قوم طريقها في دار الآخر فاقتسموها فليس لكل واحد أن يفتح باباً المقصورة إلى الدار، وإنما من لهم طريق على مقدار الباب ولا يكون لهم حق المرور فيما سوى الطريق، وإن كان بجنب المقصورة دار لهم وقعت في قسمة رجل فأراد أحدهم أن يجعل الطريق إلى داره في هذه المقصورة لم يكن له ذلك طريق مشترك بين جماعة ليس لواحد منهم أن يفتح باباً لدار أخرى لا حق لها في هذه الطريق. ولو اقتسموا قرية فأصاب أحدهم قراح والآخر كرم والآخر بيوت جاز بتراضيهم، وإذا اقتسما كرم وفيه عنب وثمر ينظر ؛ إن قالا على أن النصف لفلان بكل قليل وكثير وما فيه من الأعشاب والثمار فهي مقسومة وإلا فهي على الشركة بينهما. دار وفيها طريق لآخر لا يمنعها عن قسمتها ويترك طريقه على عرض الباب العظمى، فإن باعوا الدار والطريق برضاهم ضرب صاحب الدار على مثلي ثمن الطريق وصاحب الممر بثلث الثمن لأن الطريق بينهم أثلاثاً إذا لم يعلم قدر الأنصباء فيكون الثمن بينهم أثلاثاً، وكذا إذا كان رقبة الطريق لاثنين وللآخر حق المرور. ومن مات منهم وتعددت ورثته اعتبر حقه كحق واحد، وإن لم يعرف أن الدار ميراث بينهم فالطريق على عدد الرؤوس وقسمة الطريق على عدد الرؤوس . ولو كان فيها طريق من ناحية وطريق لآخر من ناحية أخرى يعزل لهما طريق واحدة A governor divided a house and left a public path. The city belongs to the Muslims. Later, he wants to give part of the path to a neighbor for a canopy. Is this permissible?

The Legal Nature of Tahaayu: Acknowledgment, not Exchange
Explaining the nature, conditions, and rulings of tahaayu in places and slave service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fiqh classifies tahaayu as iqraar (acknowledgment) rather than mubaadalah (exchange) and identify the conditions that distinguish it.

Core Idea
Tahaayu is acknowledgment, not exchange — thus avoiding riba and allowing temporary use without transfer of ownership.

This lesson unpacks the foundational distinction that makes tahaayu permissible. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that tahaayu in a single house is a form of acknowledgment, not an exchange of usufruct, which would be invalid under riba rules. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
Tahaayu in a single house: each co-owner uses a part. The passage states it is iqraar (acknowledgment), not mubaadalah (exchange).
This classification determines permissibility and conditions.
2
Analyze the underlying concern
Why might it be problematic? Exchange of usufruct in a single genus risks riba (usury) because values may differ.
Hanafi law prohibits exchange of two goods of the same genus without equality.
3
Apply the Hanafi solution
The school reclassifies it as iqraar, a unilateral concession, not a bilateral exchange. This avoids riba issues.
Iqraar means each owner yields his share momentarily, not transfers it.
4
Note the conflicting opinion
Some say it is partly loan; the text refutes this because tahaayu is binding, unlike loan which is revocable.
Loan ('ariyah) is non-binding; tahaayu is binding once agreed.
5
Derive the ruling
Therefore, tahaayu in place is permissible without a time limit, and it is not invalidated by death of either party.
The text explicitly mentions these consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعبيد يعتبر مبادلة من كل وجه حتى لا يجوز من غير رضاهم. وفي الكافي : ولا يبطل التهايؤ بموت أحدهما ولا بموتهما ا هـ . ولو طلب أحد الشريكين القسمة والآخر المهايأة يقسم القاضي لأنه أبلغ ولو وقع التهايؤ فيما يحتمل القسمة ثم طلب أحدهما القسمة يقسم ويبطل التهايؤ لأنه أبلغ، أما إذا تهايا في سكنى دار واحدة على أن يسكن أحدهما بعضها والآخر البعض أو أحدهما العلو والآخر السفل جازت لأن القسمة على هذا الوجه جائزة فكذا التهايؤ وهو إقرار لا مبادلة لأنها لا تجوز في الجنس الواحد الربا. وقيل: هو إقرار من وجه عارية من وجه ولا يخفى أن كلا القولين مشكل لأن كل واحد منهما يترك ماله من المنفعة فيما أخذه صاحبه بعوض وهو الانتفاع بنصيب صاحبه فكيف يتصور أن يكون إقراراً في الكل أو عارية في البعض والعارية غير لازمة والمهايأة لازمة؟ فإن قيل جمع المنافع الشائعة في السن في بيت واحد محلل لعدم جواز انتقال العرض من محل إلى محل آخر فكيف يمكن القاضي جمعها؟ فالجواب أن المراد ليس للقاضي أن يجمعها حقيقة حتى يتوجه ما ذكر، بل المراد أن القاضي يعتبرهما جميعاً ضرورة والأوجه أنه إقرار من كل وجه في التهايؤ في المكان ولهذا لا يشترط التأقيت وفي المهايأة في الزمان إقرار من كل وجه. ولو أشغل أحدهما نصيبه جاز شرط في المهايأة أو لم يشترط لأنه يجوز المهايأة في الاشتغال حال الانفراد فيجوز تبعاً للمهايأة في السكنى؛ كذا في المحيط . ولو نهاياً في دارين جاز ويجبر الآبي عنها ويعتبر إفرازاً كالأعيان المتفاوتة، فلو وضع أحدهما في داره شيئاً أو ربط فيها دابة فعثر به إنسان ومات لا يضمن، ولو بنى أو حفر فيها بئراً ضمن لأن الأول من مرافق السكني حتى يملكه المستعير فلا يكون متعدياً في نصيب شريكه فلا يضمن وفي البناء والحفر يكون في مقدار نصيب شريكه فيضمن ولا يضمن مقدار نصيبه . ولو تهايآ في دارين على أن يسكن كل واحد منهما داراً أو يؤجرها وإن زادت غلة أحدهما لا يشارك الآخر في الفضل . والفرق أن في الدارين أمكن تصحيح قسمة المنفعة حقيقة، ولو تهايأ في الزمان في الخدمة عبداً جاز لأنها متعينة فيه لتعذر التهايؤ في المكان والبيت الصغير كالعبد. ولو اختلفا في التهايؤ من حيث الزمان والمكان في محل يحتملهما يأمرهم القاضي بالاتفاق، فإن اختاروا من حيث الزمان يقرع في البداية تطييباً لقلوبهما ونفياً للتهمة عن نفسه، ولو تهايآ في عبدين على الخدمة جاز، أما عندهما فظاهر لأن قسمة الرقيق جائزة عندهما فكذا المنفعة. وأما عند الإمام فروي عنه أنها لا تجوز إلا بالتراضي لأن قسمة الرقيق لا يجري فيها الجبر عنده فكذا المهاياة . والأصح أن القاضي يهايؤ بينهما جبراً بطلب أحدهما لأن المنافع من حيث الخدمة قلما تتفاوت بخلاف أعيان الرقيق لأنها تتفاوت تفاوتاً فاحشاً على ما بينا ولو نهاياً على أن نفقة كل عبد على من يخدمه جاز استحساناً لأن العادة جرت بالتسامح فيها بخلاف كسوة المماليك لأنها لا تسامح فيها عادة.
And slaves are considered exchange from every aspect such that it is not permissible without their consent. In al-Kafi: And tahaayu is not invalidated by the death of one of them nor by the death of both. And if one of the two partners requests division and the other requests tahaayu, the judge enforces division because it is more effective. And if tahaayu occurs in something that admits division, then one of them requests division, he is granted division and the tahaayu is invalidated because it is more effective. As for when they make tahaayu in residing in one house, such that one lives in a part and the other in another part, or one in the upper floor and the other in the lower floor, it is permissible because division in this manner is permissible, and thus tahaayu is also permissible. And it is acknowledgment (iqraar), not exchange, because exchange is not permissible in a single genus due to riba. And it is said: it is acknowledgment from one aspect and loan from another aspect, and it is not hidden that both statements are problematic because each of them leaves his usufruct for that which his partner takes in exchange, which is the benefit from the partner's share. So how can it be imagined that it is entirely acknowledgment or partially loan, while loan is non-binding and tahaayu is binding? If it is said: the collection of common usufructs in milk in a single house is analyzable due to the impermissibility of transferring an attribute from one place to another, so how can the judge collect them? The answer is that what is meant is not that the judge collects them in reality such that what was mentioned is directed; rather, what is meant is that the judge considers both of them necessarily. And the correct view is that it is acknowledgment from every aspect in tahaayu in place, and for this reason temporariness is not a condition, and in tahaayu in time it is acknowledgment from every aspect. And if one of them occupies his share, it is permissible whether a condition was stipulated in the tahaayu or not, because tahaayu in occupation is permissible when alone, so it is permissible as a consequence of tahaayu in residence. Thus in al-Muhit. And if they make tahaayu in two houses, it is permissible and the one who refuses is compelled, and it is considered segregation like dissimilar non-fungibles. So if one of them places something in his house or ties an animal there, and a human stumbles over it and dies, he is not liable. But if he builds or digs a well there, he is liable because the first type is from the amenities of residence such that the borrower owns it, so he is not transgressing in the share of his partner and thus not liable, whereas in building and digging, he is in the amount of his partner's share so he is liable, and he is not liable for his own share. And if they make tahaayu in two houses with the condition that each lives in a house or rents it out, even if the produce of one increases, the other does not share in the excess. The difference is that in two houses it is possible to correct the division of usufruct in reality. And if one makes tahaayu in time for the service of a slave, it is permissible because the benefit is specified therein due to the impossibility of tahaayu in place, and a small house is like a slave. And if they differ in tahaayu from the perspective of time and place in a location that admits both, the judge orders them to agree. If they choose from the perspective of time, he draws lots at the beginning to please their hearts and to remove suspicion from himself. And if they make tahaayu in two slaves for service, it is permissible. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent because division of slaves is permissible according to them, so too is usufruct. As for Imam Abu Hanifa, it is narrated from him that it is not permissible except with mutual consent because division of slaves does not involve compulsion according to him, so too tahaayu. And the most correct is that the judge imposes tahaayu between them by compulsion upon the request of one of them because the benefits in terms of service rarely differ, unlike the physical slaves themselves because they differ greatly as we have explained. And if they agree that the maintenance of each slave is upon the one who uses his service, it is permissible by istihsan because custom is to be lenient in that, unlike clothing of slaves because there is no leniency in that customarily.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rulings on tahaayu (temporary division of use) in the Hanafi school. The author begins by addressing the nature of tahaayu in relation to slaves, stating that it is considered an exchange in all respects, hence requiring the slaves' consent. However, the relied-upon view in the madhhab is that tahaayu is acknowledgment (iqraar), not exchange, making it permissible even without the slaves' consent in cases of property. The passage then contrasts tahaayu with formal division (qismah), noting that a judge will enforce division if one partner demands it because it is a more definitive resolution. The discussion moves to tahaayu in residence: it is valid in a single house where each occupies a distinct part, treating it as acknowledgment rather than exchange. A critical point is that tahaayu in place does not require a fixed time limit, whereas in time it does. The text addresses objections about the impossibility of collecting common usufructs, clarifying that the judge does not physically collect them but recognizes the arrangement necessarily. Further, the passage covers liability for damages: if one partner places objects or ties an animal in his allocated area, he is not liable for accidents; but building or digging a well makes him liable because it encroaches on the partner's share. In the case of two houses, tahaayu is valid and partners can even let them out, with any excess in rent not shared. The latter part focuses on tahaayu in slave service. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow it, even by compulsion, because the benefits of service are nearly equal. Abu Hanifa requires mutual consent due to the principle that division of slaves is not compelled. The accepted view (mufta bihi) is that the judge can compel tahaayu in service. Lastly, expenses for maintenance during tahaayu are governed by custom: feeding the slave is on the user, but clothing is not included unless agreed.

Key Terms
التهايؤ (al-tahaayu): A mutual agreement between co-owners to alternately use the common property in time or place, considered a form of acknowledgment (iqraar) in the Hanafi school.
الإقرار (al-iqraar): Acknowledgment that each co-owner retains ownership of his share but yields possession to the other for a period, without transferring ownership.
المبادلة (al-mubaadalah): Exchange; the view that tahaayu is an exchange of usufruct which would be invalid if it involves riba in a single genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal nature of tahaayu in the residence of a single house?
A) It is an exchange of usufruct (mubaadalah) requiring equality.
B) It is a binding loan ('ariyah) from one partner to another.
C) It is acknowledgment (iqraar) by each partner of the other's right to the allocated portion.
D) It is a sale of the share of usufruct for a fixed period.

Key Takeaway
Tahaayu in a single property is a valid acknowledgment, not an exchange, thus avoiding riba and allowing flexible temporary use.

Tahaayu in Houses: Rules, Compulsion, and Liability
Explaining the nature, conditions, and rulings of tahaayu in places and slave service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules of tahaayu in residential property including the conditions for validity, the effect of requesting division, and the liability for damages in the allocated area.

Core Idea
In two houses, tahaayu is enforceable even unwillingly; liability for damages depends on whether the act is normal use or structural change.

This lesson dives into the practical rules of tahaayu as applied to houses. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq distinguishes between tahaayu in a single house (mutual consent, iqraar) and tahaayu in two houses (compulsory, segregation). It also sets out liability rules: placing objects or tying animals does not cause liability, but building or digging a well does, because it encroaches on the partner's share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Tahaayu in a single house vs. two houses. The passage gives different rules for each.
Single house: iqraar, no compulsion. Two houses: considered segregation, compulsion allowed.
2
Analyze the effect of requesting formal qismah
If one partner demands formal division, the judge grants it and tahaayu is invalidated because division is more effective.
This applies even if tahaayu was initially agreed upon.
3
Examine liability for acts in the allocated area
Placing objects or tying an animal: no liability because these are normal amenities of residence. Building or digging: liability for the partner's share because it alters property.
The key is whether the act is customary use or a physical alteration.
4
Apply the ruling for two houses
If they make tahaayu in two houses, it is permissible and the recalcitrant partner is compelled. They can even rent out their respective houses, and the excess rent is not shared.
This is treated as an effective division of usufruct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعبيد يعتبر مبادلة من كل وجه حتى لا يجوز من غير رضاهم. وفي الكافي : ولا يبطل التهايؤ بموت أحدهما ولا بموتهما ا هـ . ولو طلب أحد الشريكين القسمة والآخر المهايأة يقسم القاضي لأنه أبلغ ولو وقع التهايؤ فيما يحتمل القسمة ثم طلب أحدهما القسمة يقسم ويبطل التهايؤ لأنه أبلغ، أما إذا تهايا في سكنى دار واحدة على أن يسكن أحدهما بعضها والآخر البعض أو أحدهما العلو والآخر السفل جازت لأن القسمة على هذا الوجه جائزة فكذا التهايؤ وهو إقرار لا مبادلة لأنها لا تجوز في الجنس الواحد الربا. وقيل: هو إقرار من وجه عارية من وجه ولا يخفى أن كلا القولين مشكل لأن كل واحد منهما يترك ماله من المنفعة فيما أخذه صاحبه بعوض وهو الانتفاع بنصيب صاحبه فكيف يتصور أن يكون إقراراً في الكل أو عارية في البعض والعارية غير لازمة والمهايأة لازمة؟ فإن قيل جمع المنافع الشائعة في السن في بيت واحد محلل لعدم جواز انتقال العرض من محل إلى محل آخر فكيف يمكن القاضي جمعها؟ فالجواب أن المراد ليس للقاضي أن يجمعها حقيقة حتى يتوجه ما ذكر، بل المراد أن القاضي يعتبرهما جميعاً ضرورة والأوجه أنه إقرار من كل وجه في التهايؤ في المكان ولهذا لا يشترط التأقيت وفي المهايأة في الزمان إقرار من كل وجه. ولو أشغل أحدهما نصيبه جاز شرط في المهايأة أو لم يشترط لأنه يجوز المهايأة في الاشتغال حال الانفراد فيجوز تبعاً للمهايأة في السكنى؛ كذا في المحيط . ولو نهاياً في دارين جاز ويجبر الآبي عنها ويعتبر إفرازاً كالأعيان المتفاوتة، فلو وضع أحدهما في داره شيئاً أو ربط فيها دابة فعثر به إنسان ومات لا يضمن، ولو بنى أو حفر فيها بئراً ضمن لأن الأول من مرافق السكني حتى يملكه المستعير فلا يكون متعدياً في نصيب شريكه فلا يضمن وفي البناء والحفر يكون في مقدار نصيب شريكه فيضمن ولا يضمن مقدار نصيبه . ولو تهايآ في دارين على أن يسكن كل واحد منهما داراً أو يؤجرها وإن زادت غلة أحدهما لا يشارك الآخر في الفضل . والفرق أن في الدارين أمكن تصحيح قسمة المنفعة حقيقة، ولو تهايأ في الزمان في الخدمة عبداً جاز لأنها متعينة فيه لتعذر التهايؤ في المكان والبيت الصغير كالعبد. ولو اختلفا في التهايؤ من حيث الزمان والمكان في محل يحتملهما يأمرهم القاضي بالاتفاق، فإن اختاروا من حيث الزمان يقرع في البداية تطييباً لقلوبهما ونفياً للتهمة عن نفسه، ولو تهايآ في عبدين على الخدمة جاز، أما عندهما فظاهر لأن قسمة الرقيق جائزة عندهما فكذا المنفعة. وأما عند الإمام فروي عنه أنها لا تجوز إلا بالتراضي لأن قسمة الرقيق لا يجري فيها الجبر عنده فكذا المهاياة . والأصح أن القاضي يهايؤ بينهما جبراً بطلب أحدهما لأن المنافع من حيث الخدمة قلما تتفاوت بخلاف أعيان الرقيق لأنها تتفاوت تفاوتاً فاحشاً على ما بينا ولو نهاياً على أن نفقة كل عبد على من يخدمه جاز استحساناً لأن العادة جرت بالتسامح فيها بخلاف كسوة المماليك لأنها لا تسامح فيها عادة.
And slaves are considered exchange from every aspect such that it is not permissible without their consent. In al-Kafi: And tahaayu is not invalidated by the death of one of them nor by the death of both. And if one of the two partners requests division and the other requests tahaayu, the judge enforces division because it is more effective. And if tahaayu occurs in something that admits division, then one of them requests division, he is granted division and the tahaayu is invalidated because it is more effective. As for when they make tahaayu in residing in one house, such that one lives in a part and the other in another part, or one in the upper floor and the other in the lower floor, it is permissible because division in this manner is permissible, and thus tahaayu is also permissible. And it is acknowledgment (iqraar), not exchange, because exchange is not permissible in a single genus due to riba. And it is said: it is acknowledgment from one aspect and loan from another aspect, and it is not hidden that both statements are problematic because each of them leaves his usufruct for that which his partner takes in exchange, which is the benefit from the partner's share. So how can it be imagined that it is entirely acknowledgment or partially loan, while loan is non-binding and tahaayu is binding? Checkpoint
In tahaayu of a single house, if one partner builds a wall in his allocated area, what is his liability?
A) He is liable for the value of the wall.
B) He is liable for the value of the partner's share that was occupied by the wall.
C) He is liable for the entire house.
D) He is not liable because he owns his share.

Tahaayu in Slave Service: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the nature, conditions, and rulings of tahaayu in places and slave service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions within the Hanafi school regarding compulsion in tahaayu for slave service and evaluate the reasoning behind the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn allow the judge to compel tahaayu in slave service; Imam Abu Hanifa requires mutual consent – but the relied-upon view is the Sahibayn's.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether tahaayu in the service of slaves can be imposed by a judge. The passage contrasts Imam Abu Hanifa's analogy to the indivisibility of the slaves themselves with the Sahibayn's focus on the near equality of service benefits. The text concludes that the Sahibayn's view is the most correct, and it is the basis for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Is tahaayu in the service of two slaves enforceable by the judge without the consent of both partners?
This is a practical question: one partner wants tahaayu, the other refuses.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
He holds it is not permissible without mutual consent, analogizing to the rule that division of slaves themselves is not compelled.
Slaves are considered indivisible for compulsion because of potential large differences in value.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow compulsion because division of slaves is permissible according to their view, and service usufruct is usually equal.
They consider the usufruct as separate from the physical slave.
4
Analyze the tarjih rationale
The text prefers the Sahibayn's view because the benefits of service rarely vary, whereas the physical slaves themselves can differ greatly.
The underlying cause (illah) for prohibiting compulsion in division of slaves—difference in value—does not apply to their service.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

As for when they make tahaayu in residing in one house, such that one lives in a part and the other in another part, or one in the upper floor and the other in the lower floor, it is permissible because division in this manner is permissible, and thus tahaayu is also permissible. And it is acknowledgment (iqraar), not exchange, because exchange is not permissible in a single genus due to riba. And it is said: it is acknowledgment from one aspect and loan from another aspect, and it is not hidden that both statements are problematic because each of them leaves his usufruct for that which his partner takes in exchange, which is the benefit from the partner's share. So how can it be imagined that it is entirely acknowledgment or partially loan, while loan is non-binding and tahaayu is binding? If it is said: the collection of common usufructs in milk in a single house is analyzable due to the impermissibility of transferring an attribute from one place to another, so how can the judge collect them? The answer is that what is meant is not that the judge collects them in reality such that what was mentioned is directed; rather, what is meant is that the judge considers both of them necessarily. And the correct view is that it is acknowledgment from every aspect in tahaayu in place, and for this reason temporariness is not a condition, and in tahaayu in time it is acknowledgment from every aspect. And if one of them occupies his share, it is permissible whether a condition was stipulated in the tahaayu or not, because tahaayu in occupation is permissible when alone, so it is permissible as a consequence of tahaayu in residence. Thus in al-Muhit. And if they make tahaayu in two houses, it is permissible and the one who refuses is compelled, and it is considered segregation like dissimilar non-fungibles. So if one of them places something in his house or ties an animal there, and a human stumbles over it and dies, he is not liable. But if he builds or digs a well there, he is liable because the first type is from the amenities of residence such that the borrower owns it, so he is not transgressing in the share of his partner and thus not liable, whereas in building and digging, he is in the amount of his partner's share so he is liable, and he is not liable for his own share. And if they make tahaayu in two houses with the condition that each lives in a house or rents it out, even if the produce of one increases, the other does not share in the excess. The difference is that in two houses it is possible to correct the division of usufruct in reality. And if one makes tahaayu in time for the service of a slave, it is permissible because the benefit is specified therein due to the impossibility of tahaayu in place, and a small house is like a slave. And if they differ in tahaayu from the perspective of time and place in a location that admits both, the judge orders them to agree. If they choose from the perspective of time, he draws lots at the beginning to please their hearts and to remove suspicion from himself. And if they make tahaayu in two slaves for service, it is permissible. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent because division of slaves is permissible according to them, so too is usufruct. As for Imam Abu Hanifa, it is narrated from him that it is not permissible except with mutual consent because division of slaves does not involve compulsion according to him, so too tahaayu. And the most correct is that the judge imposes tahaayu between them by compulsion upon the request of one of them because the benefits in terms of service rarely differ, unlike the physical slaves themselves because they differ greatly as we have explained. And if they agree that the maintenance of each slave is upon the one who uses his service, it is permissible by istihsan because custom is to be lenient in that, unlike clothing of slaves because there is no leniency in that customarily.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rulings on tahaayu (temporary division of use) in the Hanafi school. The author begins by addressing the nature of tahaayu in relation to slaves, stating that it is considered an exchange in all respects, hence requiring the slaves' consent. However, the relied-upon view in the madhhab is that tahaayu is acknowledgment (iqraar), not exchange, making it permissible even without the slaves' consent in cases of property. The passage then contrasts tahaayu with formal division (qismah), noting that a judge will enforce division if one partner demands it because it is a more definitive resolution. The discussion moves to tahaayu in residence: it is valid in a single house where each occupies a distinct part, treating it as acknowledgment rather than exchange. A critical point is that tahaayu in place does not require a fixed time limit, whereas in time it does. The text addresses objections about the impossibility of collecting common usufructs, clarifying that the judge does not physically collect them but recognizes the arrangement necessarily. Further, the passage covers liability for damages: if one partner places objects or ties an animal in his allocated area, he is not liable for accidents; but building or digging a well makes him liable because it encroaches on the partner's share. In the case of two houses, tahaayu is valid and partners can even let them out, with any excess in rent not shared. The latter part focuses on tahaayu in slave service. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow it, even by compulsion, because the benefits of service are nearly equal. Abu Hanifa requires mutual consent due to the principle that division of slaves is not compelled. The accepted view (mufta bihi) is that the judge can compel tahaayu in service. Lastly, expenses for maintenance during tahaayu are governed by custom: feeding the slave is on the user, but clothing is not included unless agreed.

Key Terms
التهايؤ (al-tahaayu): A mutual agreement between co-owners to alternately use the common property in time or place, considered a form of acknowledgment (iqraar) in the Hanafi school.
الإقرار (al-iqraar): Acknowledgment that each co-owner retains ownership of his share but yields possession to the other for a period, without transferring ownership.
الجبر (al-jabr): Compulsion by the judge to enforce a tahaayu arrangement when one co-owner refuses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, can a judge compel tahaayu in the service of two slaves?
A) No, because slaves are indivisible and require consent.
B) Yes, because service benefits are usually equal.
C) Yes, but only if the slaves are of equal physical value.
D) No, because tahaayu is always voluntary.

Key Takeaway
Compulsion in tahaayu for slave service is the mufta bihi, justified by the near equality of service benefits, overriding the analogy to indivisible physical slaves.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Purification by Slaughter: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on purification by slaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on purification by slaughter, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the analogy of tanning.

Core Idea
Slaughter purifies both meat and skin of inedible animals — it removes impure fluids like tanning.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the effect of slaughter (dhabh) on the purity of meat and skin of animals whose meat is not eaten. The Hanafi school holds that slaughter purifies both, while al-Shafi'i argues that it only affects permissibility and cannot purify the skin independently. Understanding this dispute reveals deeper principles about the nature of ritual slaughter and the relationship between primary and derivative rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: slaughter of an animal not eaten purifies its meat and skin, except human and pig.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that al-Shafi'i argues slaughter primarily affects permissibility of meat; skin purification is derivative and cannot exist without the primary, analogous to Magian slaughter which has no effect.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Understand the Hanafi qiyas: slaughter removes impure fluids (like blood), purifying the skin just as tanning does. The effect on skin is an independent objective.
The argument type is qiyas khafi (analogical reasoning based on an underlying effective cause).
4
Examine sub-disputes
Consider the sub-dispute on using purified products for non-eating purposes, and the intra-Hanafi narration that only skin (not meat) is purified.
The preferred view is that both meat and skin are purified.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis can use the skin without tanning; Shafi'is require tanning even after slaughter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وذبح ما لا يؤكل لحمه يطهر لحمه وجلده إلا الآدمي والخنزير) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى : الذكاة لا تؤثر في جميع ذلك لأن أثر الذكاة في إباحة اللحم أصل وفي طهارته وطهارة الجلد تبع ولا تبع بدون الأصل فصار نظير ذبح المجوس . ولنا أن الذكاة مؤثرة في إزالة الرطوبات النجسة فإذا زالت طهرت كما في الدباغ، وهذا الحكم مقصود في الجلد كالتناول في اللحم وفعل المجوسي غير معتد به فلا بد من الدباغ، وكما يطهر لحمه يطهر شحمه أيضاً حتى لو وقع في الماء القليل لا يفسده. وهل يجوز الانتفاع به لغير الأكل؟ قيل لا يجوز اعتباراً بالأكل، وقيل يجوز كالزيت إذا خالطه شحم الميتة والزيت غالب فإنه ينتفع به في غير الأكل. والخنزير لا يؤثر فيه الدباغ لنجاستة والآدمي لكرامته وفي روايتة لا يطهر بالذكاة لحم ما لا يؤكل لحمه والجلد يطهر هو الصحيح وقد مر في كتاب الطهارة اهـ .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And slaughter of what is not eaten for meat purifies its meat and its skin except the human and the pig.) And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Slaughter has no effect on all that, because the effect of slaughter is primarily on the permissibility of the meat, and on its purity and the purity of the skin as a derivative, and there is no derivative without the primary, so it becomes similar to the slaughter of a Magian. And our proof is that slaughter is effective in removing the impure fluids, so when they are removed it becomes pure, as in tanning. And this ruling is intended for the skin just as consumption is intended for the meat. And the action of the Magian is not considered, so tanning is necessary. And just as its meat is purified, its fat is also purified, such that if it falls into a small amount of water it does not spoil it. And is it permissible to benefit from it for other than eating? It is said no, by analogy with eating, and it is said yes, like oil if rendered fat of a dead animal is mixed with it and the oil is predominant, then it can be used for other than eating. And the pig is not affected by tanning due to its impurity, and the human due to his honor. And in one narration: the meat of what is not eaten for meat is not purified by slaughter, but the skin is purified, that is correct. And it has passed in the book of purification. End.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether slaughter (dhabh) of an animal whose meat is not eaten (like a mule or donkey) purifies its meat and skin. The Hanafi position, represented by the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, states that it does purify, except for human and pig. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that slaughter only affects permissibility of meat, and skin purification is derivative, so it cannot be purified without the meat being permissible, comparing it to slaughter by a Magian. The Hanafi response is that slaughter removes impure fluids (like blood), thus purifying, analogous to tanning. The purification of skin is a direct objective, just as consumption is for meat. The Hanafis also note that the Magian's slaughter is invalid, so tanning is still needed. Further, the fat is also purified; if it falls into water, it doesn't spoil it. There is a sub-dispute on using such purified products for non-eating purposes: some say no, others analogize to oil mixed with dead animal fat where the oil predominates. The exceptions remain: pig (impure in essence) and human (honored). A narration mentions that meat is not purified, but skin is, and that is the correct view.

Key Terms
الذكاة (al-dhakāh): The ritual slaughter of an animal in the prescribed Islamic manner.
الدباغ (al-dibāgh): Tanning of animal skin to purify it, used as an analogy for purification by slaughter.
المجوس (al-majūs): Magians (Zoroastrians); their slaughter is not considered valid in Hanafi fiqh, so it does not purify.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the effect of slaughtering an animal like a mule on its fat (شحم) if it falls into a small amount of water?
A) It makes the water najis and it must be discarded.
B) It does not spoil the water because the fat is purified by slaughter.
C) It depends on whether the fat is predominant.
D) It is only purified if the meat is also permissible to eat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that slaughter purifies inedible animals completely (except human/pig) because it removes impure fluids, analogous to tanning.

The Ten Signs of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah
Defining Ahl al-Sunnah through two sets of ten characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two lists of ten characteristics that define Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah and explain their function as signs, not obligations.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunnah is defined by ten specific beliefs and practices, including prayer in congregation, respecting Companions, and prayer behind every imam.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh work provides two complementary lists of ten signs by which a person may know they are upon the Sunnah and the Community. Understanding these signs is foundational for recognizing the saved sect and avoiding innovation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first list from Ibn Umar
Read the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar and note the ten signs the Prophet (peace be upon him) enumerates. Pay attention to the order and wording.
This list is attributed directly to the Prophet.
2
Identify the second list from Al-Hawi
Read the ten characteristics listed in Al-Hawi. Compare them with the first list to see commonalities and differences.
The second list includes beliefs about the Quran and the precedence of the four caliphs.
3
Note the conditions from al-Kashshaf
Read the note from the author of al-Kashshaf stating that there are additional conditions for the Hanafi school that must be observed.
This hints that the lists are not exhaustive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يتصل به فصل يشتمل على السنة والجماعة المضمرات وروي عن علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله تعالى عنه أنه قال : المؤمن إذا أوجب السنة والجماعة استجاب الله دعاءه وقضى حوائجه وغفر له الذنوب جميعاً وكتب له براءة من النار وبراءة من النفاق. وفي خبر عبد الله بن عمر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : كان على السنة والجماعة استجاب الله دعاءه وكتب له بكل خطوة من يخطوها عشر حسنات ورفع له عشر درجات فقيل له : يا رسول الله متى يعلم الرجل أنه أهل السنة والجماعة ؟ فقال : إذا وجد في نفسه عشرة أشياء فهو على السنة الجماعة : أن يصلي الصلوات الخمس بالجماعة، ولا يذكر أحداً من الصحابة بسوء وينقصه، ولا يخرج على السلطان بالسيف، ولا يشك في إيمانه، ويؤمن بالقدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى، ولا يجادل في دين الله تعالى، ولا يكفر أحداً من أهل التوحيد بذنب، ولا يدع الصلاة على من من أهل القبلة، ويرى المسح على الخفين جائزاً في السفر والحضر، ويصلي خلف كل إمام براً وفاجر. وفي الحاوي : من أهل السنة والجماعة من فيه عشرة أشياء، : الأول أن لا يقول شيئاً في الله تعالى لا يليق بصفاته. والثاني يقر بأن القرآن كلام الله تعالى وليس بمخلوق . والثالث يرى الجمعة والعيدين خلف كل بر وفاجر والرابع يرى القدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى. والخامس يرى المسح على الخفين جائزاً. والسادس لا يخرج على الأمير بالسيف. والسابع يفضل أبا بكر وعمر وعثمان وعلياً على سائر الصحابة والثامن لا يكفر أحداً من أهل القبلة بذنب والتاسع يصلي على من مات من أهل القبلة العاشر يرى الجماعة رحمة والفرقة عذاباً. قال صاحب الكشاف في هذا الفصل شروط وزيادات لأصحابنا يجب أن تراعى. وسئل أبو النصر الدبوسي عن معنى قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «كل مولود يولد على الفطرة» (۱) قال : أي يولد على دلالة الخلقة على معنى أن الله تعالى خلقه على خلقة لو نظر إليها وتفكر فيها على حسب ما يجب لدلته على ربوبيته ووحدانيته. ومعنى قوله «يهودانه» أي ينقلانه إلى حكم اليهودية وأحوالها بالتلقين لكونه في أيديهم لذلك ظهر العمل في المسألتين عن سلف أن الولد يكون تابعاً للوالدين من غير من أن يكون منه كفر أو إسلام على الحقيقة. وسئل أبو النصر الدبوسي فقيل : ما معنى الأخبار التي رويت عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وروي في بعضها صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر وفي بعضها القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة إن مرضوا فلا تعودوهم وإن ماتوا فلا تشيعوا جنائزهم (۲) وفي بعضها إن أمتي ستفترق على كذا وكذا كلهم في النار إلا واحدة (۳) فقال المشايخ: إن من شرائط السنة والجماعة أن لا يكفر أحد من أهل القبلة. وسئل بعضهم عن الفاجر والبر فقال : الفاجر هو الفاسق من أهل الإسلام. العدل هو من أهل الإسلام وقد جاء مفسراً عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال «لا يخرج أحد من أهل الإسلام بذنب وذكر افتراق الأديان بالأهواء فمن كان من أهل الإسلام فالصلاة خلفه جائزة وإن كان يعلم الكبائر وأهل الأهواء على ضربين منهم من يخرج عن الإسلام، لا ومنهم من يخرج. فمن خرج عن الإسلام لا تجوز الصلاة خلفه وقد سبق الكلام فيه مستوفى في تتمة كلمات الكفر في آخر كلمات الكفر في آخر كتاب السير وفي باب الجماعة : ومن لا يخرج منه فالصلاة خلفه جائزة، ومن خرج من الإسلام فهو في النار خالد، ومن لم يخرج منه فهو في جملة أهل المشيئة قال الله تعالى إن الله لا يغفر أن يشرك به ويغفر ما دون ذلك لمن يشاء [النساء : ٤٨] وأما ما جاء في حق أهل الأهواء أنهم لا يعادون ولا تشيع
And connected to it is a chapter that includes the Sunnah and the Community (al-Jama'ah) and the contracting ones [?]. It was narrated from Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: The believer, if he affirms the Sunnah and the Community, Allah answers his prayer, fulfills his needs, forgives all his sins, and writes for him a certificate of freedom from the Fire and a certificate of freedom from hypocrisy. And in the report of Abdullah ibn Umar from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: He who is upon the Sunnah and the Community, Allah answers his prayer and writes for him for every step he takes ten good deeds and raises him ten degrees. So it was said to him: O Messenger of Allah, when does a man know that he is a person of the Sunnah and the Community? He said: If he finds in himself ten things, he is upon the Sunnah and the Community: that he performs the five prayers in congregation, does not mention any of the Companions with evil or diminish them, does not rebel against the ruler with the sword, does not doubt his faith, believes in predestination, its good and evil from Allah Almighty, does not argue in the religion of Allah, does not excommunicate any of the people of tawhid for a sin, does not abandon prayer over anyone who dies from the people of the qibla, considers wiping over the leather socks permissible in travel and residence, and prays behind every imam, whether pious or impious. And in al-Hawi: Among the people of the Sunnah and the Community are those in whom are ten things: First, that he does not say anything about Allah that is unbefitting His attributes. Second, he affirms that the Quran is the speech of Allah and is not created. Third, he considers the Friday prayer and the two Eid prayers permissible behind every pious and impious person. Fourth, he believes predestination, its good and evil, is from Allah. Fifth, he considers wiping over the leather socks permissible. Sixth, he does not rebel against the ruler with the sword. Seventh, he gives preference to Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali over the rest of the Companions. Eighth, he does not excommunicate anyone from the people of the qibla for a sin. Ninth, he prays over anyone who dies from the people of the qibla. Tenth, he considers the community a mercy and division a punishment. The author of al-Kashshaf said: In this chapter there are conditions and additions for our companions that must be observed. And Abu al-Nasr al-Dabusi was asked about the meaning of his saying, peace be upon him, 'Every child is born upon the fitrah.' He said: i.e., born upon the indication of the creation, meaning that Allah created him upon a disposition that, if he looked at it and reflected upon it as is necessary, would lead him to His Lordship and Oneness. And the meaning of his saying, 'his parents make him a Jew,' i.e., they transfer him to the judgment of Judaism and its states by teaching him, because he is in their hands. Therefore, the practice in the two issues appeared from the predecessors that the child is a follower of the parents, without there actually being disbelief or faith from him. And Abu al-Nasr al-Dabusi was asked, and it was said: What is the meaning of the reports narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, and in some of them it is reported: Pray behind every pious and impious person, and in some of them: The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation; if they are sick, do not visit them; and if they die, do not attend their funerals, and in some of them: Indeed my nation will split into so many sects, all of them are in the Fire except one. So the scholars said: Indeed among the conditions of the Sunnah and the Community is that one does not excommunicate anyone from the people of the qibla. And some of them were asked about the impious and the pious, and he said: The impious is the sinful one from among the people of Islam. The just one is from the people of Islam. And it has come explained from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, he said: 'No one from the people of Islam leaves Islam because of a sin.' And he mentioned the division of religions by desires. So whoever is from the people of Islam, praying behind him is permissible, even if he commits major sins. And the people of desires are of two types: some of them leave Islam, and some of them do not. So whoever leaves Islam, praying behind him is not permissible. And the discussion about this has already been covered in full in the appendix on words of disbelief at the end of the Book of Siyar. And in the Chapter on Congregation: And whoever does not leave Islam, praying behind him is permissible. And whoever leaves Islam, he is in the Fire forever. And whoever does not leave it, he is under the will of Allah. Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (4:48). And as for what has come regarding the people of desires, that they are not to be visited and not to be accompanied [in funerals]...
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling that outlines the characteristics of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah according to Hanafi understanding. It begins by citing a narration from Ali ibn Abi Talib emphasizing the virtues of affirming the Sunnah and the Community: answered prayers, forgiveness, and freedom from the Fire and hypocrisy. Then a longer hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar lists ten practical signs for a person to know if he is upon the Sunnah and the Community. These include praying the five daily prayers in congregation, not speaking ill of any Companion, not rebelling against the ruler, not doubting one's faith, believing in divine predestination, not arguing in religion, not excommunicating any Muslim for sin, performing funeral prayers for all people of the qibla, considering wiping over leather socks permissible, and praying behind every imam, whether pious or impious. The text then provides another list from the work Al-Hawi, which similarly enumerates ten characteristics, with slight variations: not attributing unbefitting qualities to Allah, affirming the Quran as uncreated speech, considering Friday and Eid prayers permissible behind both pious and impious rulers, believing in predestination, allowing wiping over socks, not rebelling against rulers, preferring the four rightly guided caliphs over other Companions, not excommunicating any Muslim for sin, praying over any deceased person of the qibla, and viewing community as mercy and division as punishment. A note is added from the author of al-Kashshaf that there are additional conditions for the Hanafi school that must be observed. The passage then turns to questions raised to Abu al-Nasr al-Dabusi. First, the hadith 'every child is born upon the fitrah' is explained: fitrah means the natural disposition that, if reflected upon properly, leads to recognition of the Creator. 'Parents make him a Jew' means they transfer him to Judaism by teaching; hence the child follows the parents in worldly legal rulings, but no actual disbelief or faith is ascribed to the child. Second, the apparent contradiction between hadiths commanding prayer behind every pious and impious ruler and other hadiths condemning Qadariyya (a sect) and warning about sectarian division is resolved. The scholars state that a condition of Ahl al-Sunnah is not to excommunicate anyone from the people of the qibla. The terms 'fajir' (impious) and 'barr' (pious) are defined: fajir is a sinful Muslim, barr is a righteous Muslim. A hadith confirms that no Muslim leaves Islam due to sin alone. Therefore, prayer behind a sinful Muslim is permissible, even if he commits major sins. The people of desires (ahl al-ahwa') are divided into two categories: those who leave Islam (by holding beliefs that take them out of the faith) and those who do not. Prayer behind one who does not leave Islam is valid; behind one who does leave Islam (i.e., becomes an apostate) it is invalid. The passage concludes by citing the Quranic verse that those who do not commit shirk are under Allah's will for forgiveness, while those who leave Islam are in the Fire eternally. The incomplete last sentence suggests that people of desires who remain within Islam are not to be visited when sick or attended at funerals, consistent with other hadith warnings.

Key Terms
السنة والجماعة (al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah): The saved sect in Islam, following the prophetic way and the consensus of the early community; defined by specific beliefs and practices as enumerated in the text.
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks during ablution, considered permissible in travel and residence.
الفاجر (al-fājir): The sinful person from among the people of Islam, who commits major sins but does not leave the fold of Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar, which of the following is NOT one of the ten signs?
A) Praying the five prayers in congregation.
B) Considering wiping over leather socks permissible.
C) Preferring Abu Bakr and Umar over other Companions.
D) Not rebelling against the ruler with the sword.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah is defined by ten specific signs that encompass core beliefs and practices, with the understanding that these are indicators, not the entirety of faith.
