When Desire Changes the Ruling: Lowering the Gaze
Explains the condition of desire and its effect on the ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the presence of desire alters the ruling on same-gender looking and apply the rule to scenarios involving doubt.

Core Idea
If desire is present or even suspected, the gaze must be lowered immediately.

Building on the general rule, this lesson focuses on the critical condition of desire. The passage details how desire changes the ruling from permissible to prohibited, and even discusses cases of doubt. Understanding this nuance is essential for practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenarios Involving Desire
The text describes three cases: clear desire (شهوة), dominant opinion that one desires, and doubt (شك).
In all three, the ruling is that she must lower her gaze.
2
Compare with Opposite Gender
Note that for a man looking at a woman's face/hands, if he fears temptation (خوف), he must also lower his gaze. The difference is that women's desire is considered more prevalent.
The text explains that if a man desires, it is two-sided; if a woman desires, it is one-sided. Two-sided desire is more dangerous.
3
Apply the Rule to Doubtful Situations
If there is doubt about whether desire is present, the ruling is precautionary: lower the gaze.
This is based on the principle of blocking the means to sin (sadd al-dhara'i').
4
Relate to the General Principle
The overall principle is that any same-gender looking that is likely to lead to fitnah becomes haram.
Connection to the earlier condition of safety from desire.

Source Text

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: How Much Can a Woman See of Another Woman?
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on what a woman may see of another woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations within the Hanafi school on what parts a woman may see of another woman, explain the evidence for each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one allows all non-awrah, the other restricts back and belly; the first is mufta bihi.

While the general rule permits same-gender looking, there is a notable internal dispute within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa has two narrations on how much a woman may see of another woman. This lesson unpacks that dispute and explains why the broader view is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Narrations
First narration: a woman may look at another woman's non-awrah parts (like a man looking at a man). Second narration: a woman is like a man looking at his mahram, so she cannot see the back and belly.
The text presents both, then declares the first as al-asahh.
2
Examine the Evidence for Each
First: qiyas on men looking at men, custom, and necessity. Second: analogy to mahram looking at woman.
The second narration's basis is that a woman's back and belly are considered like 'awrah in this context.
3
Analyze the Tarjih (Preference)
The author states the first narration is the most correct (al-asahh) and implicitly the mufta bihi.
This tarjih is based on the strength of the evidence and practicality.
4
Determine the Practical Consequence
Under the first narration, women can see each other's backs and bellies. Under the second, they cannot.
This difference affects the ruling on entering bathhouses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله تعالى: (والمرأة للمرأة والرجل للرجل) وهذا هو القسم الرابع من التقسيمات، ومعناه المرأة للمرأة والرجل للرجل يعني نظر المرأة إلى المرأة كنظر الرجل إلى الرجل حتى يجوز للمرأة أن تنظر منها إلى ما يجوز للرجل أن ينظر إليه من الرجل إذا أمنت الشهوة والفتن لأن ما ليس بعورة لا يختلف فيه الرجال والنساء فكان لها أن تنظر منه ما ليس بعورة، وإن كان في قلبها شهوة أو أكبر رأيها أنها تشتهي أو شكت . في لها أن تغض بصرها، ولو كان الرجل هو الناظر إلى ما يجوز له منها كالوجه والكف لا ينظر إليه حتماً مع الخوف لأنه محرم عليه والفرق أن الشهوة عليهن أغلب وهي كالمتحقق حكماً فإذا اشتهى الرجل كانت الشهوة موجودة من الجانبين، وإذا اشتهت لم توجد إلا منها فكانت جانب واحد، والموجود من الجانبين أقوى في الإفضاء إلى الوقوع وإنما جاز ما ذكرنا للمجانسة وانعدام الشهوة غالباً كما في نظر الرجل إلى الرجل، وكذا الضرورة قد تحققت فيما بينهن. وعن الإمام أن تنظر المرأة إلى المرأة كنظر الرجل إلى محارمه فلا يجوز لها أن تنظر إلى الظهر والبطن في هذه الرواية بخلاف نظرها إلى الرجل لأن الرجل يحتاج إلى زيادة الانكشاف، وفي الرواية الأولى يجوز وهو الأصح ما جاز للرجل أن ينظر إليه من الرجل جاز مسه لأنه ليس بعورة ولا يخاف منه الفتنة . قال في النهاية : وهذا دليل على أنهن لا يمنعن دخول الحمام لأن العرف ظاهر به في جميع البلدان وبناء الحمامات للنساء وحاجة النساء إلى الحمام فوق حاجة الرجال لأن المقصود من دخوله الزينة والمرأة إلى هذا أحوط من الرجال ويمكن للرجل دخول الأنهار والحياض والمرأة لا تتمكن من ذلك غالباً .اهـ. وحكي أن الإمام دخل الحمام فرأى رجلاً مكشوف العورة يقال له بطرطا وكان رجلاً متكلماً فغض أبو حنيفة بصره فقال له العاصي : مذكم أعمى الله بصرك؟ قال : مذهتك الله سترك اهـ. وفي الكافي : وعظم الساق ليس بعورة .اهـ.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And the woman for the woman and the man for the man) This is the fourth division of the divisions. Its meaning is: woman for woman and man for man, meaning the woman's looking at a woman is like the man's looking at a man, so it is permissible for a woman to look from her at what is permissible for a man to look at from a man if she is safe from desire and temptation, because what is not 'awrah does not differ between men and women, so she may look at what is not 'awrah from her. But if there is desire in her heart, or her dominant opinion is that she desires, or she doubts, then she must lower her gaze. And if a man is looking at what is permissible for him from her, like the face and hands, he does not look at it necessarily if there is fear, because it is unlawful for him. The difference is that desire is more prevalent in women, and it is considered as if it is realized in terms of ruling. So if a man desires, desire exists from both sides; if a woman desires, it exists only from her, so it is only one side. What exists from both sides is stronger in leading to occurrence. It is only permissible due to similarity and the absence of desire usually, as in a man looking at a man. Likewise, necessity is realized among them. And it is narrated from the Imam that a woman looks at a woman like a man looks at his mahrams, so she is not permitted to look at the back and belly in this narration, unlike her looking at a man because a man needs more exposure. In the first narration, it is permissible, and it is the most correct. Whatever is permissible for a man to look at from a man, it is permissible to touch, because it is not 'awrah and there is no fear of temptation from it. He said in al-Nihayah: This is evidence that women are not prevented from entering the bathhouse, because custom is manifest in all cities and the construction of bathhouses for women, and women's need for the bathhouse is greater than men's because the purpose of entering is adornment, and women are more in need of this than men, and a man can enter rivers and ponds but a woman is generally not able to do so. And it is narrated that the Imam entered the bathhouse and saw a man with exposed 'awrah called Batrta, and he was a speaking man. Abu Hanifah averted his gaze, and the disobedient one said to him: 'O effeminate one, has God blinded your eyes?' He said: 'O effeminate one, may God conceal you.' And in al-Kafi: The shin bone is not 'awrah.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding same-gender looking. The author first clarifies the general rule: a woman looking at another woman is analogous to a man looking at another man, meaning that it is permissible to look at those parts of the body that are not 'awrah, provided there is no desire or fear of temptation. The underlying reasoning ('illa) is that non-'awrah parts are the same for both genders, so there is no additional prohibition. However, if desire is present, the ruling changes: the woman must lower her gaze, and similarly a man must lower his gaze from a woman's permissible parts if he fears temptation. The author explains that the difference in treatment between men and women lies in the fact that desire is more prevalent and considered virtually present in women; if a man desires, desire is mutual, but if a woman desires, it is one-sided, and two-sided desire is more likely to lead to sin. Therefore, the permissibility is based on similarity and the usual absence of desire. Then the author mentions a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that a woman looking at another woman is like a man looking at his mahrams, so she cannot look at the back and belly. But the first narration (permissibility) is considered the most correct (al-asahh). The passage then extends the ruling to touching: whatever is permissible to look at is also permissible to touch. Citing al-Nihayah, the author deduces that women are allowed to enter bathhouses because custom permits it and women's need is greater. The story of Imam Abu Hanifa in the bathhouse illustrates the importance of lowering the gaze even in such settings. Finally, a note from al-Kafi clarifies that the shin bone (azm al-saq) is not 'awrah.

Key Terms
المحارم (al-maharim): Permanent unmarriageable kin (mahrams); the ruling for looking at mahrams is stricter for women.
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct; indicates the preferred view among competing narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi position regarding a woman looking at another woman's back?
A) It is not permissible because the back is like 'awrah.
B) It is permissible because the back is not 'awrah for same-gender looking.
C) It is permissible only if the viewer is a mahram.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position permits women to see each other's non-awrah parts, including back and belly, when safe from desire, despite an alternative restrictive narration.

Touching What Is Permissible to Look At: General Rule and Proofs
General principle and primary hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching mahrams and explain the primary hadith proofs that support it.

Core Idea
If looking is allowed, touching is also allowed—except when desire is feared.

This lesson explores the foundational principle that permission to look implies permission to touch, as taught by the Hanafi school. We examine the proofs from the Prophet's own practice and his direct teachings, including the important distinction between mahram and non-mahram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The matn states: 'And he may touch what it is permissible for him to look at.' Identify the category of persons covered: mahrams and men, not foreign women.
2
Examine the proof from practice
The Prophet kissed Fatima's head and praised her. This shows that physical contact with mahrams is not only allowed but can be a sign of affection and piety.
3
Analyze the seclusion hadith
The hadith 'A man should not be alone with a woman with whom there is no relationship' implies that with mahrams (who are of relation) it is allowed. Understand the exception: when fear of desire exists.
4
Apply the hadith on zina of limbs
The hadith warns that each limb has its form of zina. This strengthens the need to avoid even the slightest unlawful touch, but conversely shows that permissible touch (without desire) is not zina.
5
Conclude the ruling
The overall ruling: touching mahrams is mubah with the condition of safety from desire. If desire is feared, it becomes haram. The principle is derived from these proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ويمس ما يحل له النظر إليه) يعني يجوز أن ما حل له النظر إليه من محارمه ومن الرجل لا من الأجنبية لتحقق الحاجة إلى ذلك من المسافرة والمخالطة، وكان عليه الصلاة والسلام يقبل رأس فاطمة ويقول أجد منها ريح الجنة وقال «من قبل رأس أمه فكأنما قبل عتبه الجنة» ولا بأس بالخلوة معها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا يخلون رجل بامرأة ليس منها سبيل فإن ثالثهما الشيطان» والمراد إذا لم تكن محرماً لأن المحرم بسبيل منها إلا إذا خاف على نفسه أو عليها الشهوة فحينئذ لا يمسها ولا ينظر إليها ولا يخلو بها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «العينان تزنيان وزناهما النظر واليدان تزنيان وزناهما البطش، والرجلان تزنيان وزناهما المشي، والفرج يصدق ذلك أو يكذبه» فكان في كل واحد منها زنا والزنا محرم أنواعه بجميع وحرمه الزنا بالمحارم أشد وأغلظ فيجتنب الكل ولا بأس بالمسافرة بهن لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا تسافر المرأة فوق ثلاثة أيام إلا بزوج أو محرم» وإن احتاجت إلى الإركاب والإنزال فلا بأس أن يمسها من وراء ثيابها ويأخذ ظهرها وبطنها من وراء إذا أمنا الشهوة، وإن خاف عليها أو على نفسه أو ظناً أو شكاً فليجتنب ذلك بجهده، فإن أمكنها الركوب بنفسها تمتنع من ذلك أصلاً، وإن لم يمكنها تتلفف بالثياب كي لا تصل حرارة عضوها إلى عضوه، وإن لم تجد الثياب فليدفع عن نفسه بقدر الإمكان. ولا بأس بأن يدخل على الزوجين محارمهما وهما في الفراش من غير وطء باستئذان وكذا الخادم حين يخلو الرجل بأهله، وكذا الأمة ويكره أن يأخذها بيده ويدخلها ويعلم الناس أنه يريدها اهـ. (فروع) قال في الجامع الصغير ويكره تقبيل غيره ومعانقته ولا بأس بالمصافحة لما أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام سئل أيقبل بعضنا بعضاً ؟ قال : لا. قالوا: ويعانق بعضنا بعضاً؟ قال: لا. قالوا : أيصافح بعضنا بعضاً؟ قال : نعم . قال مشايخنا: إن كان يأمن على من الشهوة وقصد البر والإكرام وتعظيم المسلم فلا بأس به والحديث محمول على هذا التفصيل المصافحة سنة قديمة متوارثة وفي النوادر : وتقبيل يد العالم والسلطان العادل لا بأس به لما روي عن سفيان أنه قال : تقبيل يد العالم والسلطان العادل سنة. وفي جامع الجوامع ولا بأس أن تمس الأمة الرجل وتغمزه وتدهنه ما لم يشته إلا ما بين السرة والركبة . وفي التتارخانية : ولم يذكر محمد في شيء من الكتب الخلوة والمسافرة بإماء الغير وقد اختلفوا فيه ؛ فمنهم من قال لا يحل وإليه مال الحاكم الشهيد، ومنهم من قال يحل وبه قال الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي، والذين قالوا بالحل اختلفوا فيما بينهم بعضهم قال ليس له أن يعالجها في النزول والركوب وبعضهم قال له ذلك إن أمن على نفسه الشهوة عليها. وفي الغياثية والغلام الذي بلغ الشهوة كالبالغ والكافر كالمسلم؛ هذا الذي ذكرناه إذا كانت شابة، فإن كانت عجوزاً قال في التتارخانية : فإن كانت عجوزاً لا تشتهي فلا بأس بمصافحتها ومس يدها وأن تغمز رجله، وكذا إذا كان شيخاً يأمن على نفسه وعليها. وفي الغياثية : ولا بأس أن يعانقها من وراء الثياب إلا أن تكون ثيابها رقيقة تصل حرارة بدنها إليه وفيما إذا كان الماس هو المرأة قال : إن كانت ممن لا يجامع مثلها ولا يجامع مثله فلا بأس بالمصافحة فليتأمل عند الفتوى فإن كانت صغيرة لا تشتهى أو لا يشتهى مثلها فلا بأس بالنظر إليها ومسها.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And he may touch what it is permissible for him to look at). Meaning: It is permissible that whatever is permissible for him to look at among his mahrams and from a man, not from a foreign woman, due to the confirmed need for that in traveling and mixing. The Prophet, peace be upon him, used to kiss the head of Fatima and say 'I find from her the scent of Paradise' and said 'Whoever kisses his mother's head, it is as if he kissed the threshold of Paradise.' There is no harm in seclusion with her due to his saying: 'A man should not be alone with a woman with whom there is no relationship, for verily the third of them is Satan.' What is meant is when she is not a mahram, because the mahram is of his relation, except if he fears desire for himself or for her, then he should not touch her, nor look at her, nor be alone with her, due to his saying: 'The two eyes commit zina and their zina is looking; the two hands commit zina and their zina is touching; the two feet commit zina and their zina is walking; and the private parts confirm or deny that.' So in each of them there is zina, and zina is forbidden in all its types, and the prohibition of zina with mahrams is more severe and strict, so he should avoid all. There is no harm in traveling with them due to his saying: 'A woman should not travel more than three days except with a husband or mahram.' If she needs to be mounted and dismounted, there is no harm in touching her from outside her garments and taking her back and belly from behind if they are safe from desire. If he fears for her or for himself, even by assumption or doubt, he should avoid that with his effort. If she can mount by herself, he should refrain from that entirely. If she cannot, she should wrap herself in clothes so that the heat of her limb does not reach his limb. If she cannot find clothes, then he should push away as much as possible. There is no harm in a mahram entering upon a married couple while they are in bed without intercourse with permission, and likewise a servant when a man is alone with his wife, and likewise a female slave. It is disliked that he take her by hand and bring her in and make people know that he desires her. (Branches): In al-Jami' al-Saghir it is said: It is disliked to kiss other than [one's spouse/parents?] and to embrace, and there is no harm in shaking hands, because the Prophet was asked 'Should some of us kiss others?' He said: 'No.' They said: 'Should some of us embrace others?' He said: 'No.' They said: 'Should some of us shake hands with others?' He said: 'Yes.' Our scholars said: If he feels safe from desire and intends piety, honor, and exaltation of the Muslim, then there is no harm. The hadith is interpreted with this detail. Shaking hands is an ancient established sunnah. In al-Nawadir: Kissing the hand of a scholar and a just ruler is not blameworthy, because it is narrated from Sufyan that he said: Kissing the hand of a scholar and a just ruler is a sunnah. In Jami' al-Jawami': There is no harm in a female slave touching a man and rubbing him and applying oil, as long as he does not desire, except between the navel and the knee. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Muhammad did not mention in any of the books seclusion and traveling with the female slaves of others, and they differed concerning it. Some said it is not permissible, and al-Hakim al-Shahid inclined to this. Some said it is permissible, and Imam Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi held this view. Those who said permissible differed among themselves: some said he may not assist her in dismounting and mounting; some said he may do so if he feels safe from desire. In al-Ghiyathiyyah: A boy who has reached the age of desire is like a mature person, and a disbeliever is like a Muslim. This is if she is young. If she is an old woman, al-Tatarkhaniyyah said: If she is an old woman who is not desired, there is no harm in shaking her hand and touching her hand and his rubbing her foot, and likewise if he is an old man who feels safe from himself and from her. In al-Ghiyathiyyah: There is no harm in embracing her from behind garments, unless her garments are thin so that the heat of her body reaches him. As for when the toucher is a woman, he said: If she is not of those who have intercourse like her, nor of those with whom intercourse is had, then there is no harm in shaking hands. So one should reflect when giving fatwa. If she is a young girl who is not desired or whose like is not desired, then there is no harm in looking at her and touching her.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn ruling 'and he may touch what it is permissible to look at'. It begins by establishing the general principle: permissible looking implies permissible touching. This applies to mahrams (blood or marriage relatives) and to men (i.e., a man can touch another man), but not to a foreign woman. The need for such contact arises in travel and daily interaction. The text then adduces several proofs. First, prophetic practice: the Prophet kissed his daughter Fatima's head and praised her. Second, prophetic hadith encouraging kissing one's mother's head. Third, the principle of seclusion: the Prophet forbade a man from being alone with a non-mahram woman, indicating that with mahrams it is allowed (unless fear of desire). Fourth, the hadith describing the 'zina' of the eyes, hands, feet, and private parts, warning that each part has its form of unlawful action. This underscores the need to avoid even the pretext of zina, especially with mahrams where the prohibition is stronger. The text then gives practical rulings: traveling with mahrams is allowed, but physical contact in mounting/dismounting should be minimized and done through thick clothing, only when safe from desire. If there is even doubt, it should be avoided. For a mahram entering upon a couple in bed, it is permitted with permission, but it is disliked to take the female slave by hand and make it public. The 'Branches' (furu') section discusses specific cases: kissing and embracing others (non-mahrams, non-spouses) is disliked; shaking hands with Muslims is permissible, with the condition of safety from desire and good intention. The hadith that prohibited kissing/embracing but permitted handshake is interpreted as applying to situations where desire is feared. Kissing the hand of a scholar or just ruler is permissible and considered a sunnah. With female slaves of others, there is ikhtilaf: some allow seclusion and travel, some not, with conditions. For old women who are not desired, touching and handshake are allowed. Similarly, for children who are not yet objects of desire, touching is allowed. The overall theme is that permissibility hinges on absence of desire and genuine need.

Key Terms
محرم (maḥram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, allowing interaction without strict hijab rules.
خلوة (khalwa): Privacy between a man and a woman who are legally permitted to be alone (e.g., mahram or spouses).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary condition that turns permissible touching of a mahram into prohibited?
A) The absence of a third person.
B) The presence or fear of sexual desire.
C) The mahram being a woman.
D) The touch being during travel.

Key Takeaway
Touching mahrams is permissible by default, but becomes prohibited the moment desire is present or genuinely feared.

Travel and Physical Contact: Conditions and Precautionary Measures
Conditions for physical contact during travel and interaction with mahrams and servants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for physical contact with mahrams during travel and describe the required precautions to avoid unlawful touch.

Core Idea
Permissible touch during travel is strictly regulated to avoid any possible desire, with a hierarchy of precautions from barriers to complete avoidance.

This lesson delves into the specific rulings for traveling with mahrams, where physical contact is often inevitable. The text lays out a detailed code of conduct: from permissible touch through barriers to strict avoidance when even doubt arises. We also examine the rulings on entering upon a married couple and the limits with servants.

Guided Path
1
Establish the general permissibility of travel
The text begins with the hadith that a woman may travel more than three days only with a mahram. This affirms that travel with mahram is allowed and implies physical help is necessary.
2
Understand the hierarchy of precautions
The text lists: (1) If she can mount by herself, avoid all touch. (2) If not, touch over thick garments, and only back/belly from behind. (3) If garments are thin, wrap extra cloth. (4) If no cloth, minimize contact as much as possible. Each step aims to eliminate direct skin contact.
3
Apply the condition of safety from desire
All these measures assume both are safe from desire. If there is any fear, even a doubt, the text says 'avoid with effort' (falyajtanib dhalika bijuhdihi). This elevates the ruling to haram.
4
Examine the rulings on entering upon a couple and with servants
It is permissible for a mahram to enter upon a married couple in bed with permission. Similarly, a servant may enter when the husband is alone with his wife. But it is disliked for a man to take a female slave by hand and publicly show his intention.
5
Summarize the overall rule
The underlying principle is: permissibility is tied to necessity and absolute safety from desire. Any suspicion or doubt shifts the ruling toward prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ويمس ما يحل له النظر إليه) يعني يجوز أن ما حل له النظر إليه من محارمه ومن الرجل لا من الأجنبية لتحقق الحاجة إلى ذلك من المسافرة والمخالطة، وكان عليه الصلاة والسلام يقبل رأس فاطمة ويقول أجد منها ريح الجنة وقال «من قبل رأس أمه فكأنما قبل عتبه الجنة» ولا بأس بالخلوة معها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا يخلون رجل بامرأة ليس منها سبيل فإن ثالثهما الشيطان» والمراد إذا لم تكن محرماً لأن المحرم بسبيل منها إلا إذا خاف على نفسه أو عليها الشهوة فحينئذ لا يمسها ولا ينظر إليها ولا يخلو بها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «العينان تزنيان وزناهما النظر واليدان تزنيان وزناهما البطش، والرجلان تزنيان وزناهما المشي، والفرج يصدق ذلك أو يكذبه» فكان في كل واحد منها زنا والزنا محرم أنواعه بجميع وحرمه الزنا بالمحارم أشد وأغلظ فيجتنب الكل ولا بأس بالمسافرة بهن لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا تسافر المرأة فوق ثلاثة أيام إلا بزوج أو محرم» وإن احتاجت إلى الإركاب والإنزال فلا بأس أن يمسها من وراء ثيابها ويأخذ ظهرها وبطنها من وراء إذا أمنا الشهوة، وإن خاف عليها أو على نفسه أو ظناً أو شكاً فليجتنب ذلك بجهده، فإن أمكنها الركوب بنفسها تمتنع من ذلك أصلاً، وإن لم يمكنها تتلفف بالثياب كي لا تصل حرارة عضوها إلى عضوه، وإن لم تجد الثياب فليدفع عن نفسه بقدر الإمكان. ولا بأس بأن يدخل على الزوجين محارمهما وهما في الفراش من غير وطء باستئذان وكذا الخادم حين يخلو الرجل بأهله، وكذا الأمة ويكره أن يأخذها بيده ويدخلها ويعلم الناس أنه يريدها اهـ. (فروع) قال في الجامع الصغير ويكره تقبيل غيره ومعانقته ولا بأس بالمصافحة لما أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام سئل أيقبل بعضنا بعضاً ؟ قال : لا. قالوا: ويعانق بعضنا بعضاً؟ قال: لا. قالوا : أيصافح بعضنا بعضاً؟ قال : نعم . قال مشايخنا: إن كان يأمن على من الشهوة وقصد البر والإكرام وتعظيم المسلم فلا بأس به والحديث محمول على هذا التفصيل المصافحة سنة قديمة متوارثة وفي النوادر : وتقبيل يد العالم والسلطان العادل لا بأس به لما روي عن سفيان أنه قال : تقبيل يد العالم والسلطان العادل سنة. وفي جامع الجوامع ولا بأس أن تمس الأمة الرجل وتغمزه وتدهنه ما لم يشته إلا ما بين السرة والركبة . وفي التتارخانية : ولم يذكر محمد في شيء من الكتب الخلوة والمسافرة بإماء الغير وقد اختلفوا فيه ؛ فمنهم من قال لا يحل وإليه مال الحاكم الشهيد، ومنهم من قال يحل وبه قال الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي، والذين قالوا بالحل اختلفوا فيما بينهم بعضهم قال ليس له أن يعالجها في النزول والركوب وبعضهم قال له ذلك إن أمن على نفسه الشهوة عليها. وفي الغياثية والغلام الذي بلغ الشهوة كالبالغ والكافر كالمسلم؛ هذا الذي ذكرناه إذا كانت شابة، فإن كانت عجوزاً قال في التتارخانية : فإن كانت عجوزاً لا تشتهي فلا بأس بمصافحتها ومس يدها وأن تغمز رجله، وكذا إذا كان شيخاً يأمن على نفسه وعليها. وفي الغياثية : ولا بأس أن يعانقها من وراء الثياب إلا أن تكون ثيابها رقيقة تصل حرارة بدنها إليه وفيما إذا كان الماس هو المرأة قال : إن كانت ممن لا يجامع مثلها ولا يجامع مثله فلا بأس بالمصافحة فليتأمل عند الفتوى فإن كانت صغيرة لا تشتهى أو لا يشتهى مثلها فلا بأس بالنظر إليها ومسها.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And he may touch what it is permissible for him to look at). Meaning: It is permissible that whatever is permissible for him to look at among his mahrams and from a man, not from a foreign woman, due to the confirmed need for that in traveling and mixing. The Prophet, peace be upon him, used to kiss the head of Fatima and say 'I find from her the scent of Paradise' and said 'Whoever kisses his mother's head, it is as if he kissed the threshold of Paradise.' There is no harm in seclusion with her due to his saying: 'A man should not be alone with a woman with whom there is no relationship, for verily the third of them is Satan.' What is meant is when she is not a mahram, because the mahram is of his relation, except if he fears desire for himself or for her, then he should not touch her, nor look at her, nor be alone with her, due to his saying: 'The two eyes commit zina and their zina is looking; the two hands commit zina and their zina is touching; the two feet commit zina and their zina is walking; and the private parts confirm or deny that.' So in each of them there is zina, and zina is forbidden in all its types, and the prohibition of zina with mahrams is more severe and strict, so he should avoid all. There is no harm in traveling with them due to his saying: 'A woman should not travel more than three days except with a husband or mahram.' If she needs to be mounted and dismounted, there is no harm in touching her from outside her garments and taking her back and belly from behind if they are safe from desire. If he fears for her or for himself, even by assumption or doubt, he should avoid that with his effort. If she can mount by herself, he should refrain from that entirely. If she cannot, she should wrap herself in clothes so that the heat of her limb does not reach his limb. If she cannot find clothes, then he should push away as much as possible. There is no harm in a mahram entering upon a married couple while they are in bed without intercourse with permission, and likewise a servant when a man is alone with his wife, and likewise a female slave. It is disliked that he take her by hand and bring her in and make people know that he desires her. (Branches): In al-Jami' al-Saghir it is said: It is disliked to kiss other than [one's spouse/parents?] and to embrace, and there is no harm in shaking hands, because the Prophet was asked 'Should some of us kiss others?' He said: 'No.' They said: 'Should some of us embrace others?' He said: 'No.' They said: 'Should some of us shake hands with others?' He said: 'Yes.' Our scholars said: If he feels safe from desire and intends piety, honor, and exaltation of the Muslim, then there is no harm. The hadith is interpreted with this detail. Shaking hands is an ancient established sunnah. In al-Nawadir: Kissing the hand of a scholar and a just ruler is not blameworthy, because it is narrated from Sufyan that he said: Kissing the hand of a scholar and a just ruler is a sunnah. In Jami' al-Jawami': There is no harm in a female slave touching a man and rubbing him and applying oil, as long as he does not desire, except between the navel and the knee. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Muhammad did not mention in any of the books seclusion and traveling with the female slaves of others, and they differed concerning it. Some said it is not permissible, and al-Hakim al-Shahid inclined to this. Some said it is permissible, and Imam Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi held this view. Those who said permissible differed among themselves: some said he may not assist her in dismounting and mounting; some said he may do so if he feels safe from desire. In al-Ghiyathiyyah: A boy who has reached the age of desire is like a mature person, and a disbeliever is like a Muslim. This is if she is young. If she is an old woman, al-Tatarkhaniyyah said: If she is an old woman who is not desired, there is no harm in shaking her hand and touching her hand and his rubbing her foot, and likewise if he is an old man who feels safe from himself and from her. In al-Ghiyathiyyah: There is no harm in embracing her from behind garments, unless her garments are thin so that the heat of her body reaches him. As for when the toucher is a woman, he said: If she is not of those who have intercourse like her, nor of those with whom intercourse is had, then there is no harm in shaking hands. So one should reflect when giving fatwa. If she is a young girl who is not desired or whose like is not desired, then there is no harm in looking at her and touching her.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn ruling 'and he may touch what it is permissible to look at'. It begins by establishing the general principle: permissible looking implies permissible touching. This applies to mahrams (blood or marriage relatives) and to men (i.e., a man can touch another man), but not to a foreign woman. The need for such contact arises in travel and daily interaction. The text then adduces several proofs. First, prophetic practice: the Prophet kissed his daughter Fatima's head and praised her. Second, prophetic hadith encouraging kissing one's mother's head. Third, the principle of seclusion: the Prophet forbade a man from being alone with a non-mahram woman, indicating that with mahrams it is allowed (unless fear of desire). Fourth, the hadith describing the 'zina' of the eyes, hands, feet, and private parts, warning that each part has its form of unlawful action. This underscores the need to avoid even the pretext of zina, especially with mahrams where the prohibition is stronger. The text then gives practical rulings: traveling with mahrams is allowed, but physical contact in mounting/dismounting should be minimized and done through thick clothing, only when safe from desire. If there is even doubt, it should be avoided. For a mahram entering upon a couple in bed, it is permitted with permission, but it is disliked to take the female slave by hand and make it public. The 'Branches' (furu') section discusses specific cases: kissing and embracing others (non-mahrams, non-spouses) is disliked; shaking hands with Muslims is permissible, with the condition of safety from desire and good intention. The hadith that prohibited kissing/embracing but permitted handshake is interpreted as applying to situations where desire is feared. Kissing the hand of a scholar or just ruler is permissible and considered a sunnah. With female slaves of others, there is ikhtilaf: some allow seclusion and travel, some not, with conditions. For old women who are not desired, touching and handshake are allowed. Similarly, for children who are not yet objects of desire, touching is allowed. The overall theme is that permissibility hinges on absence of desire and genuine need.

Key Terms
محرم (maḥram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, allowing interaction without strict hijab rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a man prohibited from helping a mahram woman mount/dismount?
A) When she is able to do it herself.
B) When he fears desire for her.
C) When she is not wearing thick clothing.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Physical help to a mahram during travel is permissible only when necessary, with barriers, and with absolute confidence in absence of desire.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
12 min
Branches on Greetings, Handshakes, and Specific Categories
Branches on greetings, handshakes, and special categories including old women, children, slaves, and non-Muslims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and disliked forms of physical greeting among Muslims and evaluate the rulings for elderly, children, non-Muslims, and female slaves based on the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Handshake is a sunnah, but kissing and embracing are restricted due to the hadith of the Prophet; context and intention matter.

This lesson covers the 'furu'at' (branches) of the main ruling, applying the principles to various social interactions: shaking hands, kissing, hugging, and touching specific categories like old women, children, female slaves, and non-Muslims. It also presents an intra-madhhab difference on seclusion with female slaves of others.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the hadith on greetings
The text quotes a hadith where the Prophet prohibited kissing and embracing among Muslims in general, but allowed handshake. The commentator explains that this applies when desire is feared; otherwise, handshake is a sunnah.
2
Understand the exemption for scholars and rulers
Kissing the hand of a scholar or just ruler is considered a sunnah, derived from the practice of Sufyan al-Thawri. This is an exception to the general dislike of kissing.
3
Examine the rulings for female slaves
Touching a female slave (of others) is allowed with conditions: no desire and only below the navel and above the knee are excluded. There is ikhtilaf about seclusion and travel with them.
4
Apply age and status considerations
Old women who are not desired are treated more leniently: handshake and even rubbing feet are allowed. Similarly, children who are not yet objects of desire can be touched.
5
Summarize the overall hierarchy
The ruling on touch is not monolithic; it depends on gender, relationship, age, intention, and safety from desire. The mufti must consider all these factors.

قال رحمه الله : (ويمس ما يحل له النظر إليه) يعني يجوز أن ما حل له النظر إليه من محارمه ومن الرجل لا من الأجنبية لتحقق الحاجة إلى ذلك من المسافرة والمخالطة، وكان عليه الصلاة والسلام يقبل رأس فاطمة ويقول أجد منها ريح الجنة وقال «من قبل رأس أمه فكأنما قبل عتبه الجنة» ولا بأس بالخلوة معها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا يخلون رجل بامرأة ليس منها سبيل فإن ثالثهما الشيطان» والمراد إذا لم تكن محرماً لأن المحرم بسبيل منها إلا إذا خاف على نفسه أو عليها الشهوة فحينئذ لا يمسها ولا ينظر إليها ولا يخلو بها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «العينان تزنيان وزناهما النظر واليدان تزنيان وزناهما البطش، والرجلان تزنيان وزناهما المشي، والفرج يصدق ذلك أو يكذبه» فكان في كل واحد منها زنا والزنا محرم أنواعه بجميع وحرمه الزنا بالمحارم أشد وأغلظ فيجتنب الكل ولا بأس بالمسافرة بهن لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا تسافر المرأة فوق ثلاثة أيام إلا بزوج أو محرم» وإن احتاجت إلى الإركاب والإنزال فلا بأس أن يمسها من وراء ثيابها ويأخذ ظهرها وبطنها من وراء إذا أمنا الشهوة، وإن خاف عليها أو على نفسه أو ظناً أو شكاً فليجتنب ذلك بجهده، فإن أمكنها الركوب بنفسها تمتنع من ذلك أصلاً، وإن لم يمكنها تتلفف بالثياب كي لا تصل حرارة عضوها إلى عضوه، وإن لم تجد الثياب فليدفع عن نفسه بقدر الإمكان. ولا بأس بأن يدخل على الزوجين محارمهما وهما في الفراش من غير وطء باستئذان وكذا الخادم حين يخلو الرجل بأهله، وكذا الأمة ويكره أن يأخذها بيده ويدخلها ويعلم الناس أنه يريدها اهـ. Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn ruling 'and he may touch what it is permissible to look at'. It begins by establishing the general principle: permissible looking implies permissible touching. This applies to mahrams (blood or marriage relatives) and to men (i.e., a man can touch another man), but not to a foreign woman. The need for such contact arises in travel and daily interaction. The text then adduces several proofs. First, prophetic practice: the Prophet kissed his daughter Fatima's head and praised her. Second, prophetic hadith encouraging kissing one's mother's head. Fourth, the hadith describing the 'zina' of the eyes, hands, feet, and private parts, warning that each part has its form of unlawful action. This underscores the need to avoid even the pretext of zina, especially with mahrams where the prohibition is stronger. The text then gives practical rulings: traveling with mahrams is allowed, but physical contact in mounting/dismounting should be minimized and done through thick clothing, only when safe from desire. If there is even doubt, it should be avoided. For a mahram entering upon a couple in bed, it is permitted with permission, but it is disliked to take the female slave by hand and make it public. The overall theme is that permissibility hinges on absence of desire and genuine need.

Key Terms
محرم (maḥram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, allowing interaction without strict hijab rules.
خلوة (khalwa): Privacy between a man and a woman who are legally permitted to be alone (e.g., mahram or spouses).
إماء الغير (imā' al-ghayr): Female slaves owned by others (not by the man himself).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered a sunnah?
A) Kissing any non-mahram on the cheek as a greeting.
B) Shaking hands with a Muslim when safe from desire.
C) Embracing a male friend during travel.
D) Kissing the hand of a just ruler.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits handshake and limited touch in social contexts, with strict conditions on desire and intention, and makes exceptions for scholars, rulers, old women, and children.

Another's Female Slave as a Mahram: Ruling and Exception
Ruling with proof: another's female slave is like a mahram with an exception on belly/back, supported by Umar's action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at and touching another's female slave, identify the exception regarding her belly and back, and explain the rationale from the practice of Caliph Umar.

Core Idea
A female slave of another is like a mahram for looking and touching, except that the man may not look at her belly and back.

The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq declares that another's female slave is like a mahram, permitting a man to look at and touch her in ways normally restricted to non-mahrams. This ruling is based on necessity: she frequently goes out for errands in ordinary clothes, so her interaction with men is similar to that with mahrams. The passage supports this with an incident from Caliph Umar, who rebuked a slave woman for wearing a headcover like free women. However, the ruling is not absolute – the man may not look at her belly and back, a point debated within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Read the matn statement: 'Another's female slave is like his mahram.' Note that this applies to looking and touching, not marriage.
The ruling is permissibility (mubah) conditioned on non-exposure of certain areas.
2
Locate the evidence from Umar's practice
Find the narration of Umar punishing a slave woman for wearing a headcover. Understand that this indicates slave women should not imitate free women in full hijab, supporting the idea that they are treated like mahrams.
The objection about punishment for a permissible act is answered by the principle of preventing greater corruption.
3
Understand the objection and response
Note the objection: why punish for covering, which is permissible? The answer is discretionary punishment (ta'zir) to avoid greater corruption – if slave women appear as free women, immoral men may target free women more.
This shows the application of the legal maxim 'preventing harm takes precedence over securing benefit'.
4
Identify the exception and intra-Hanafi difference
From Al-Muhit and the commentary, note that while the female slave can look at and touch the man except between navel and knee, the man may NOT look at her belly and back. Muhammad ibn Muqatil disagreed, but the relied-upon view is the restriction.
This exception is crucial: she is like a mahram, but not identical – belly and back remain 'awrah for the male viewer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وأمة غيره كمحرمه) لأنها تحتاج إلى الخروج لحوائج مولاها في ثياب بذلة وحالها مع جميع الرجال كحال المرأة مع محارمها، كان عمر رضي الله عنه إذا رأى أمة متقنعة علاها بالدرة وقال : ألقي عنك الخمار أتتشبهين بالحرائر يا دفار . واعترض كيف عزرها على الستر الذي هو جائز والتعزير إنما يكون على ارتكاب المحظورات والمحرمات؟ وأجيب بأنه إنما فعل ذلك لأن الفساق إذا تعرضوا للحرائر كان ذلك أشد فساداً والتعرض للإماء دون ذلك في الفساد ففعل ذلك لئلا يجب الأول فيكون فيه تقليل الفساد. المحيط : ويحل للأمة النظر إلى الرجل الأجنبي إلى كل شيء منه ومسه وغمزه ما خلا في تحت السرة إلى الركبة .اهـ. ولا يجوز أن ينظر إلى بطنها وظهرها كالمحارم خلافاً لمحمد بن مقاتل فإنه يقول بالجواز .
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And the female slave of another is like his mahram) because she needs to go out for the needs of her master in shabby clothes, and her situation with all men is like the situation of a woman with her mahrams. Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, when he saw a female slave wearing a headcover, he struck her with the whip and said: 'Take off the headcover; do you imitate free women, O Dafar?' It was objected: How did he punish her for covering, which is permissible? Punishment is only for committing prohibitions and forbidden acts. It was answered: He did that only because if immoral men approach free women, that is a greater corruption, and approaching slave women is less in corruption, so he did that in order that the first might not occur, thus there is reduction of corruption. Al-Muhit: It is permissible for a female slave to look at a foreign man at everything of him, and to touch him and rub him, except what is between the navel and the knee. End. And it is not permissible to look at her belly and back, like mahrams, contrary to Muhammad ibn Muqatil who says it is permissible.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage explains the matn statement: 'Another's female slave is like his mahram.' The rationale is that a female slave goes out for her master's needs in everyday clothes (not full Islamic dress), so she is in frequent contact with men; thus her situation is similar to that of a woman with her mahrams. To support this, the text narrates an incident with Caliph Umar: he struck a female slave who wore a headcover (like free women) and commanded her to remove it. The objection is: punishment is for wrong acts, but covering is permissible, so why punish? The answer is to prevent a greater evil: if slave women appear like free women, immoral men might be more tempted to approach free women, causing greater corruption. Hence Umar's action was a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) to avoid this. Al-Muhit clarifies that a female slave may look at and touch a foreign man, except between navel and knee. However, the man may NOT look at her belly and back, even though she is like a mahram? Actually the text says 'It is not permissible to look at her belly and back, like mahrams, contrary to Muhammad ibn Muqatil.' So there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: the correct view is that her belly and back are 'awrah and not to be looked at, though she can look at him. This aligns with the principle that her 'awrah is like that of a free woman? Actually for free women, belly and back are part of 'awrah. For slave women, there is difference: they may expose more. The text seems to restrict the man's looking at her belly/back, even though she is 'like a mahram' in other respects.

Key Terms
أمة (amah): A female slave owned by another person, who goes out for errands and is in frequent contact with non-mahram men.
تعزير (ta'zīr): Discretionary punishment given by the ruler for acts that are sinful but not hadd or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Umar punish the female slave who wore a headcover?
A) Because headcover is forbidden for all women.
B) To prevent greater corruption: dressing like free women may lead to more temptation for free women.
C) Because she was a non-Muslim.
D) Because she refused to serve her master.

Key Takeaway
Another's female slave is like a mahram for looking and touching, except that the man may not look at her belly and back; this is based on the rationale of need and the practice of Caliph Umar.

Interactions with Another's Slave Woman: Mahram Status, Touching, and Display
Explains three rulings: mahram status, touching for purchase, display restrictions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi rulings on interactions with another's slave woman and explain the evidence from the practice of Umar and the principle of necessity.

Core Idea
Another's slave woman is like a mahram for hijab; necessity permits touching for purchase; she must not be displayed in a single garment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical issue in classical society: how a man interacts with a slave woman owned by someone else. The Hanafi school treats her like a mahram for hijab purposes, but with specific conditions for touching and display. Understanding these rulings clarifies the nuanced application of 'awrah and necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three distinct rulings
The passage covers: (1) another's slave woman is like a mahram for hijab; (2) a man may touch her allowable parts when intending to buy, even if he desires; (3) a mature slave woman must not be displayed for sale in a single garment. Note the reasoning and conditions.
These rulings are interconnected but have distinct proofs.
2
Analyze the evidence for the mahram-like status
The proof includes the practice of Umar (RA) who disciplined a slave woman for wearing a headcover like free women, and a rational argument: she goes out for her master's needs in worn clothes, so she is not a source of fitna like free women. An objection is raised and answered: Umar's discipline was to prevent greater evil (sinners targeting free women instead).
This is a dalil naqli (narration) and istidlal (rational inference).
3
Examine the condition of necessity for touching
When a man intends to buy a slave woman, he may touch parts that are normally permissible to look at (chest, calf, arm, head) even if he fears desire. This is permitted due to necessity (darurah) of complete inspection for purchase. The principle is that necessity overrides prohibition.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between free and slave women: for free women, such touching is not allowed.
4
Understand the display restriction
When offering a slave woman for sale, she should not be displayed in a single garment that only covers from navel to knee if she has reached puberty or the age of desire. This is because her back and belly are 'awrah and must be covered. The ruling is based on a narration from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) to prevent fitna.
The 'awrah of a slave woman in front of a foreign man is between navel and knee, but display requires full covering to avoid temptation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كمحرمه وله ذلك إذا أراد الشراء وإن اشتهى ولا تعرض الأمة إذا بلغت في إزار
مس
6
بأس به لما روي عن سفيان أنه قال : تقبيل يد العالم والسلطان العادل سنة. وفي جامع الجوامع ولا بأس أن تمس الأمة الرجل وتغمزه وتدهنه ما لم يشته إلا ما بين السرة والركبة . وفي التتارخانية : ولم يذكر محمد في شيء من الكتب الخلوة والمسافرة بإماء الغير وقد اختلفوا فيه؛ فمنهم من قال لا يحل وإليه مال الحاكم الشهيد، ومنهم من قال يحل وبه قال الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي، والذين قالوا بالحل اختلفوا فيما بينهم بعضهم قال ليس له أن يعالجها في النزول والركوب وبعضهم قال له ذلك إن أمن على نفسه الشهوة عليها. وفي الغياثية والغلام الذي بلغ الشهوة كالبالغ والكافر كالمسلم؛ هذا الذي ذكرناه إذا كانت شابة، فإن كانت عجوزاً قال في التتارخانية : فإن كانت عجوزاً لا تشتهي فلا بأس بمصافحتها ومس يدها وأن تغمز رجله، وكذا إذا كان شيخاً يأمن على نفسه وعليها. وفي الغياثية : ولا بأس أن يعانقها من وراء الثياب إلا أن تكون ثيابها رقيقة تصل حرارة بدنها إليه وفيما إذا كان الماس هو المرأة قال : إن كانت ممن لا يجامع مثلها ولا يجامع مثله فلا بأس بالمصافحة فليتأمل عند الفتوى فإن كانت صغيرة لا تشتهى أو لا يشتهى مثلها فلا بأس بالنظر إليها ومسها . قال رحمه الله: (وأمة غيره كمحرمه لأنها تحتاج إلى الخروج لحوائج مولاها في ثياب بذلة وحالها مع جميع الرجال كحال المرأة مع محارمها، كان عمر رضي الله عنه إذا رأى أمة متقنعة علاها بالدرة وقال : ألقي عنك الخمار أتتشبهين بالحرائر يا دفار . واعترض كيف عزرها على الستر الذي هو جائز والتعزير إنما يكون على ارتكاب المحظورات والمحرمات؟ وأجيب بأنه إنما فعل ذلك لأن الفساق إذا تعرضوا للحرائر كان ذلك أشد فساداً والتعرض للإماء دون ذلك في الفساد ففعل ذلك لئلا يجب الأول فيكون فيه تقليل الفساد. المحيط : ويحل للأمة النظر إلى الرجل الأجنبي إلى كل شيء منه ومسه وغمزه ما خلا في تحت السرة إلى الركبة .اهـ. ولا يجوز أن ينظر إلى بطنها وظهرها كالمحارم خلافاً لمحمد بن مقاتل فإنه يقول بالجواز . قال رحمه الله : (وله مس ذلك إذا أراد الشراء وإن اشتهى) يعني جاز له أن كل موضع بجوز له أن ينظر إليه كالصدر والساق والذراع والرأس ويقلب شعرها إذا أراد الشراء وإن خاف على الشراء فيباح له النظر والمس للضرورة وهو إرادة الشراء. وفي الشارح: أمة الرجل تكبس رجل زوجها ويخلو بها ولا يمنع من ذلك أحد، وأم الولد ا قال يمس والمدبرة والمكاتبة كالأمة لقيام الرق فيهن ووجود الحاجة والمستسعاة كالمكاتبة عند الإمام . قال رحمه الله : (ولا تعرض الأمة إذا بلغت في إزار واحد يعني إذا أراد أن يعرض أمته للبيع فلا يعرضها في إزار واحد إذا كانت بالغة. والمراد بالإزار ما ما بين السرة إلى يستر الركبة لأن ظهرها وبطنها عورة ولا يجوز كشفها، والتي بلغت حد الشهوة فهي كالبالغة لا تعرض في إزار واحد؛ روي ذلك عن محمد لوجود الاشتهاء.
Like his mahram, and he has that when he intends to buy, even if he desires, and do not display the slave woman when she has reached puberty in a single garment. ... It is permissible due to what was narrated from Sufyan: 'Kissing the hand of a scholar and a just ruler is a sunnah.' In Jami' al-Jawami': There is no harm in a slave woman touching a man, rubbing him, and applying oil to him as long as she does not desire, except between the navel and the knee. In al-Tatar Khaniyyah: Muhammad did not mention in any of the books seclusion and traveling with the slave women of others, and there is disagreement: some say it is not permissible, and al-Hakim al-Shahid inclined to that; some say it is permissible, and Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said so. Those who said permissible disagreed among themselves: some said he may not handle her in dismounting and mounting, and some said he may if he trusts himself against desire. In al-Ghiyathiyyah: A boy who has reached desire is like an adult, and a disbeliever like a Muslim. This is when she is young; if she is an old woman, in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: if she is an old woman who is not desired, there is no harm in shaking her hand, touching her hand, and having her rub his leg, and likewise if he is an old man who trusts himself and her. In al-Ghiyathiyyah: There is no harm in embracing her from behind clothes unless her clothes are thin so that her body heat reaches him. And if the toucher is the woman: if she is one who does not have intercourse with her like and he does not have intercourse with her like, there is no harm in shaking hands; consider carefully at the time of fatwa. If she is a young girl not desired or not desired by her like, there is no harm in looking at her and touching her. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And another's slave woman is like his mahram because she needs to go out for her master's needs in worn-out clothes, and her state with all men is like a woman with her mahrams.' Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) when he saw a slave woman veiled, struck her with a whip and said: 'Remove your headcover, are you imitating free women? O Dafar?' It was objected: How did he discipline her for covering, which is permissible? Discipline is only for committing prohibitions and unlawful acts? It was answered: He did that because if sinners target free women, that is worse corruption, and targeting slave women is less corruption, so he did that to prevent the greater evil, thus reducing corruption. In al-Muhit: It is permissible for a slave woman to look at a foreign man at everything of him and touch him and rub him except between the navel and the knee. End. And it is not permissible for him to look at her belly and back like mahrams, contrary to Muhammad ibn Muqatil who says permissibility. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And he may touch that when he intends to buy, even if he desires.' Meaning it is permissible for him to touch every place he may look at, like the chest, calf, arm, and head, and touch her hair when he intends to buy, even if he fears desire, because looking and touching are permitted out of necessity, which is the intention to buy. In al-Sharh: A man's slave woman may rub her husband's leg and be alone with him, and no one prevents that. And Umm al-Walad, al-Mudabbara, and al-Mukataba are like a slave woman due to slavery in them and need, and al-Mustas'ah is like al-Mukataba according to Imam Abu Hanifa. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And do not display the slave woman when she has reached puberty in a single garment.' Meaning when he wants to offer his slave woman for sale, he should not display her in a single garment if she is mature. What is meant by 'izar' is what covers from the navel to the knee, because her back and belly are 'awrah and it is not permissible to uncover them. And one who has reached the age of desire is like a mature one: not to be displayed in a single garment. That was narrated from Muhammad due to the existence of desire.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from Kitab al-Karahiyyah of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It covers three interconnected rulings about interactions with slave women owned by others. First, the general ruling that another's slave woman is legally like a mahram for a man, meaning permissible interactions are similar to those with his female mahrams, not full hijab. The proof includes the practice of Umar (RA) who disciplined a slave woman for wearing a headcover like free women, and a rational argument based on the slave woman's need to go out for work in humble clothes, making her less likely to be a source of fitna. An objection is raised and answered: Umar's discipline was to prevent greater evil (sinner targeting free women). Second, the ruling on touching when intending to buy: it is permissible to touch parts of the body that are normally permissible to look at (chest, calf, arm, head) due to necessity of purchase, even if desire is feared. This is based on the principle of necessity overriding prohibition. Third, the ruling on displaying a slave woman for sale: she should not be displayed in a single garment that only covers from navel to knee if she has reached puberty or the age of desire, because her back and belly are 'awrah and must be covered. This is from a narration of Muhammad (al-Shaybani) due to the existence of desire. The passage also includes details about old women, young girls, and different levels of desire.

Key Terms
أمة الغير (amat al-ghayr): A female slave owned by someone else, not by the man himself.
مَحْرَم (mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, so hijab rules are relaxed.
عَوْرَة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in front of non-mahrams. For a slave woman, between navel and knee is 'awrah for viewing and touching.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Permissible, because she is like a mahram and he may touch any part.

D) Permissible due to necessity for purchase, even if he desires.

Key Takeaway
Another's slave woman is like a mahram for hijab, but necessity for purchase permits touching normally prohibited parts, and she must not be displayed in a single garment when mature.

Hijab Rules for Eunuchs, Impotent Men, and Effeminate Men
Explains hijab rules for three special categories of men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hijab for eunuchs, impotent men, and effeminate men, and explain the proof from the general command of lowering the gaze.

Core Idea
Eunuchs, impotent men, and effeminate men are legally like normal men for hijab because they are males with desire.

This passage addresses a common misconception: that certain men with physical or behavioral conditions are exempt from hijab rules. The Hanafi school, however, treats them as normal men unless they are prepubescent or have no desire at all. The proof is the general command in Quran 24:30 and the narrow interpretation of the exception in 24:31.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage discusses three types of men: eunuch (khasiy), impotent man (majbub), and effeminate man (mukhannath). Understand each definition.
A eunuch has testicles removed but may still have desire; an impotent man has penis severed but may still ejaculate; an effeminate man imitates women but desires women.
2
Extract the general ruling
The passage states that all three are like a 'stallion' (normal man) regarding hijab. This means women must observe hijab in front of them just as with any non-mahram man.
3
Analyze the primary proof
The author cites Quran 24:30, the general command for believing men to lower their gaze. Since these individuals are males, they are included in the address. No exception is made for their conditions.
The exception in 24:31 for 'male attendants without desire' is interpreted narrowly.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi differences
Some earlier Hanafi scholars permitted mixing if the man has no desire (e.g., dried-up fluid or effeminate but no desire), but the correct view (al-ashahh) is prohibition due to general texts.
The passage gives two examples: the impotent man whose fluid dries up, and the effeminate man with mannerisms but desire.
5
Identify the exception
A eunuch below the age of puberty (15 years) is allowed to enter upon women because he is not yet a full male in terms of desire. This is the only exception.
Also mentioned: the 'idiot' (ablah) who has no understanding of women; the correct view is prohibition despite some permissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخصي والمجبوب والمخنث كالفحل لقوله تعالى قل للمؤمنين يغضوا من أبصارهم ﴾ [النور: ٣٠] وهم ذكور فيدخلون تحت الخطاب العام. وقالت عائشة: الخصي مثله ولا يبيع ما كان حراماً قبله ولأن الخصي ذكر يشتهي ويجامع وهو أشد جماعاً لأن آلته لا تفتر فصار كالفحل، والمجبوب ذكر يشتهي ويسحق وينزل. قال بعض المتأخرين : يسحق بفتح الياء ويسحق بضمها قال العيني : أي ينزل الماء وحكمه كأحكام الرجال في كل شيء، وقطع تلك الآلة كقطع عضو منه فلا يبيح شيئاً كان حراماً. وإن كان المجبوب قد جف ماؤه فقد رخص له بعض أصحابنا الاختلاط مع النساء لوقوع الأمن من الفتنة قال الله تعالى والتابعين غير أولي الإربة من الرجال [النور: ٣١] فقيل هو المجبوب الذي قد جف ماؤه والأصح أنه لا يحل له لعموم النصوص، وكذا المخنث وهو الذي يأتي الرديء من الأفعال لا يحل له بالاتفاق لأنه يشتهي النساء. وإن كان مخنثاً بأقواله وأفعاله متكسراً في أعضائه وليناً أ في لسانه وهو يشتهي النساء فقد رخص له بعض مشايخنا الاختلاط بالنساء. وفي الإبانة : الأصح أنه لا يحل له وقالوا الأبله الذي لا يدري ما يصنع بالنساء وإنما همه بطنه يرخص له الخلوة بالنساء والأصح له المنع ولا بأس بدخول الخصي على النساء ما لم يبلغ حد الحلم وهو خمسة عشر سنة .
And the eunuch, the impotent man, and the effeminate man are like a stallion (normal man) due to His statement: 'Tell the believing men to lower their gaze' [24:30] and they are males, so they are included under the general address. Aisha said: The eunuch is like him; he does not make permissible what was forbidden before him. And because the eunuch is a male who desires and has intercourse, and his intercourse is stronger because his organ does not tire, so he is like a stallion. And the impotent man is a male who desires and has emission and ejaculates. Some later scholars said: 'yas'u' (with فتحة on ya) and 'yas'u' (with ضمة on ya); al-Ayni said: meaning he ejaculates water. His ruling is like the rulings of men in everything, and cutting off that organ is like cutting off a limb from him, so it does not make permissible what was forbidden. If the impotent man's water has dried up, some of our associates permitted him to mix with women due to security from fitna, but Allah said 'or male attendants who are not inclined to women' [24:31], and it is said he is the impotent man whose water has dried up. The correct view is that it is not permissible for him due to the generality of the texts. Likewise, the effeminate man (mukhannath) is one who does base actions; it is not permissible for him by consensus because he desires women. If he is effeminate in his words and actions, weak in his limbs, soft in his tongue, and desires women, some of our shaykhs permitted him to be among women. In al-Ibanah: the correct view is that it is not permissible for him. They said: the idiot who does not know what to do with women, only concerned with his belly, is permitted to be alone with women, but the correct view is prohibition. There is no harm in a eunuch entering upon women as long as he has not reached the age of puberty, which is fifteen years.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof addressing the legal status of eunuchs (khasiy), impotent men (majbub), and effeminate men (mukhannath) regarding hijab rules. The Hanafi position is that all are treated as normal men (fahl) in terms of the obligation of lowering gaze and hijab, based on the general address of Quran 24:30 which includes all males. The proof is that they are males, they have desire, and in the case of eunuchs, they still have strong sexual desire (the organ does not tire). For the impotent man, even if he has no fluid, the majority Hanafi view (al-ashahh) is that he remains subject to hijab because of the general texts. Some earlier Hanafi scholars made exceptions for those with dried-up fluid, but this is rejected. For the effeminate man, even if he has effeminate mannerisms, if he still desires women, he is also subject to hijab. Only a eunuch below the age of fifteen (before puberty) is allowed to enter upon women. The passage also mentions the 'ablah' (idiot) who does not understand women; the relied-upon position is that he is also not permitted to mix with women. The overall emphasis is that these categories do not relax hijab rules unless there is certainty of no desire, and even then the correct view is prohibition.

Key Terms
الخصي (al-khasiy): A eunuch, a male whose testicles have been removed, but still has desire and can have intercourse.
المجبوب (al-majbub): An impotent male whose penis has been severed; he may still have desire and ejaculate, so he is like a normal man.
المخنث (al-mukhannath): An effeminate man, one who imitates women in speech and movement, but still desires women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the ruling on a woman appearing without hijab in front of a eunuch who has reached the age of fifteen?
A) It is permissible because eunuchs are not like normal men.
B) It is permissible only if the eunuch has no desire.
C) It is not permissible because the eunuch is like a normal man.
D) It is permissible because eunuchs are allowed to enter upon women at any age.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, eunuchs, impotent men, and effeminate men are legally equivalent to normal men for hijab rules, with the only exception being prepubescent eunuchs under fifteen.

Massage in the Bathhouse: Ruling and Conditions for Permissibility
Ruling on the disliked nature of massaging in the bathhouse and its permissible exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling on massaging body parts in the bathhouse and identify the conditions that make it permissible.

Core Idea
Massaging without necessity is disliked but becomes permissible under specific conditions of body part, relationship, and dress.

The bathhouse (hammam) is a place where physical contact often occurs. The Hanafi fiqh addresses the permissibility of such contact. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the ruling on ghamz (massage) and the conditions that transform it from disliked to permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Read the first sentence: 'غمز ذلك الأعضاء في الحمام من غير ضرورة مكروه'. State the default hukm for massaging in the bathhouse.
Default is makruh (disliked), not haram.
2
Note the permissive exceptions based on body region
Find the exceptions from al-Dhakhirah and Majmu' al-Nawazil. Which body areas are permitted?
Permitted above navel and below knee; also between them.
3
Analyze the two conditions from 'some masters'
Examine the two conditions: not washing the beard and not massaging the leg. What wisdom do they reflect?
First condition respects the owner; second respects the servant.
4
Distinguish by body part and relationship
Look at Imam Abu Bakr's distinctions: calf vs thigh, and parents vs others. What is the ruling for each?
Calf permissible, thigh disliked even over clothes.
5
Consider intention for mahram relatives
Read al-Khujandi's response regarding a man's mother. How does intention affect the ruling?
Intention of sacred respect makes it not disliked; treating as ordinary makes it disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غمز ذلك الأعضاء في الحمام من غير ضرورة مكروه. وفي الذخيرة وفي مجموع النوازل أنه يباح فيما فوق السرة ودون الركبة ويباح فيما بينهما، وبعض مشايخنا قالوا : لا بأس بذلك بشرطين : أحدهما أن لا يغسل الخادم لحيته لأن فيه إهانة صاحب اللحية، ولا يغمز رجله لأن فيه إهانة بالخادم . قال الفقيه أبو جعفر : سمعت الشيخ الإمام أبا بكر يقول : لا بأس بأن يغمز الرجل إلى الساق ويكره أن يغمز الفخذ ويمسه من وراء الثوب، وكان الإمام أبو بكر يقول : لا بأس بأن يغمز الرجل رجل والديه ولا يغمز فخذ والديه. وفي السراجية ولا بأس أن يغمز الأجنبية الرجل فوق الثياب إذا لم يكن فيه خوف الفتنة. وفي التتمة وسئل الخجندي عمن له أم هل يجوز له أن يغمز بطنها وظهرها من وراء الثياب؟ قال : إن أمسكه يعتقد حرمته كالخمر يمسكه المسلم للمسلم لا يكره، وإن أمسك يعتقد الإباحة كما لو أمسك للكافر يكره.
Massaging those body parts in the bathhouse without necessity is disliked. In al-Dhakhirah and Majmu' al-Nawazil, it is permitted above the navel and below the knee, and permitted between them. Some of our masters said: There is no harm in that with two conditions: one is that the servant should not wash his beard because that insults the owner of the beard, and should not massage his leg because that insults the servant. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: I heard the Shaykh al-Imam Abu Bakr say: There is no harm in a man massaging up to the calf, but it is disliked to massage the thigh or touch it from behind a garment. Imam Abu Bakr used to say: There is no harm for a man to massage the leg of his parents, but not their thigh. In al-Sirajiyyah, there is no harm for a non-mahram woman to massage a man over clothes if there is no fear of fitnah. In al-Tatimmah, al-Khujandi was asked about a man who has a mother: is it permissible for him to massage her stomach and back from behind clothes? He said: If he holds her sacred like wine – a Muslim holding wine for a Muslim is not disliked – and if he holds it as permissible, like holding for a disbeliever, it is disliked.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on the permissibility of massaging (ghamz) body parts in the bathhouse. It begins by stating that such massaging without necessity is makruh (disliked). However, exceptions are noted: according to al-Dhakhirah and Majmu' al-Nawazil, it is permitted above the navel and below the knee, and even between them. Some scholars add two conditions to avoid disrespect: the servant should not wash the master's beard (as that belittles the master), and should not massage the master's leg (as that belittles the servant). Imam Abu Bakr further differentiates: massaging up to the calf is fine, but the thigh is disliked, even over clothing. He also permits massaging parents' legs but not their thighs. For non-mahram women, massaging over clothes is permitted if no fitnah is feared. Finally, regarding one's mother, al-Khujandi says it depends on intention: if one treats her with sacred respect like a Muslim holding wine, it is not disliked; if one treats it as merely permissible, it is disliked.

Key Terms
غمز (ghamz): To press, massage, or touch with the hand, often in a therapeutic or cleansing context.
الفتنة (al-fitnah): Temptation or trial, particularly sexual attraction that could lead to sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Bakr, which body part is permissible to massage for a parent?
A) Thigh
B) Leg (up to calf)
C) Back
D) Head

Key Takeaway
Massaging in the bathhouse is disliked but permissible with conditions regarding body part, relationship, covering, and intention.
